Snow Clears, Drizzle Falls, Saar Vote Enthusiastic

Torches on the German Border Burned All Night

All Churches Rang Their Bells in Prayer

Victory Belongs to Germany

Saarbrücken After two days of heavy snow, a drizzle began this morning around 9:00 a.m. The roads were muddy, but voters were still enthusiastic, to the point that ballots were scarce. Villagers scrambled to take public buses and trains. In places without public transportation, voters did not hesitate to trudge through the mud on foot. Judging from the initial situation, the number of voters must be very large. In the past few days, the mutual struggles and public propaganda of the various factions have made the residents' excitement unable to be restrained. Those who are able to do so must go to vote. As of the time of dispatch, there have been no riots or irregular demonstrations. The international police force is stationed in the barracks, ready to be dispatched, but they will not be easily dispatched unless there is an emergency. Voting will end at 8:00 p.m. tonight, at which time the police force will be dispatched to escort the ballot boxes to Saarbrücken for counting. According to the observations of those familiar with the actual situation, the results of the vote will undoubtedly be that the Saar will return to Germany. However, there will also be many who want to maintain the status quo, and those who support returning to France can be said to be extremely rare. It is reported that many people have filed protests, saying that National Socialist Party members have used printed materials to distribute them to households throughout the territory to carry out intimidation. (13th Guomin Telegram)

Saarbrücken The weather is very cold, but the people of the Saar came out in droves this morning, braving the cold and gathering at the polling places in order to decide the future of their motherland. The snow on the road is quite deep. Many people walked, but even more came to the town by car. Members of the National Socialist Party shoveled snow to clear the streets, and pulled out cars that were stuck in the snow, which was convenient for pedestrians. Each polling place was extremely active, with hundreds of people waiting in line, as only four people were allowed to enter to vote each time. A sign saying "Please do not speak" was posted outside the door, and everyone obeyed, so the order was quite good. There were very few soldiers and police on the scene. Former German Prime Minister Papen arrived here this morning with his wife and two daughters to vote, waiting in the crowd for ten minutes. The most dedicated person to arrive today was a woman. She departed from Shanghai, passed through Siberia, spent sixteen days on the train, and arrived in Berlin this morning. She hired a plane to rush here to vote. Snowflakes were flying all over the city, and rumors of unrest were also spreading in the sky. However, several Reuters reporters took cars this afternoon and went to various places to inspect. Except for children picking up snow and throwing it, they did not see any disturbances. Listening to the language of the people on the road and in the taverns, I felt that the National Socialist Party was confident of winning, so even if there were disturbances, it would not damage their chances of victory. However, some people also fear that extreme opponents of the National Socialist Party will cause trouble after the vote in order to influence the League of Nations Executive Council and pass a resolution to divide the Saar's land. However, at present, there are no signs of trouble from any side. The only sound outside the polling place this morning was silence, as those waiting in line to vote stepped on each other's feet to keep warm. A Reuters reporter asked a clerk, "You don't seem to have police protection." He replied, "I don't think I need it, but if something happens, I only need to stop the voting, and the whole area will feel the trouble of having to vote again." In the afternoon, the reporter saw British soldiers reading books, writing, or playing various games to the sound of harmonicas. A soldier answered the reporter's question, saying that only one person in the team can speak German and does not understand the local dialect, but we get along very well with the residents. (13th Reuters Dispatch)

Voting Lines Calm

Saarbrücken The progress of the Saar plebiscite is very quiet, which is in contrast to the excitement of the people in recent days. From the impression of the onlookers, the voting situation can be summed up in one sentence, that is, "silence on the front lines during the plebiscite." Since this morning, voters have been pouring into polling stations everywhere like a tide, and it is likely that all procedures can be completed within one day. Everything in the polling station has been determined in advance, so it is as accurate as a mathematical formula. In front of each polling station, there is a team of National Socialist Party German Front members, wearing white armbands, and a team of Socialist and Communist Party United Front members, wearing red armbands, standing opposite each other, quiet and silent. Voters pass in front of the two teams of members, enter, and go to the voting table. Under the supervision of a neutral country official, they hand over their passport and voter registration certificate to a city council member for review. The council member gives them an envelope and a ballot, which lists three options: (1) Return to Germany, (2) Merge with France, (3) Maintain the status quo. Voters must mark a cross next to the option they choose. Any action or speech that is sufficient to indicate the voter's opinion is prohibited. After the voter makes a cross in the isolation room, they vote in the box under the supervision of the neutral country director, and then exit. Voters only need to show their voter registration certificate to ride the tram for free, so the crowding on the Saar tram is unprecedented. Since this morning, it has been snowing, and everything is white. There are no traces of police or troops on the street. All that can be seen are wooden signs placed by the German Front, covered with advertisements, stating the importance of today. In addition, the Administrative Committee decided that various publications are prohibited from being sold today. German newspapers were rushed to be sold last night. For the enemy party, spreading absurd and unfounded news, such as saying that the Vatican's official newspaper, the Roman Observer, criticized the New Saar Post, an anti-National Socialist Catholic newspaper, is completely untrue. (13th Havas Dispatch)

All Factions in High Spirits

Saarbrücken According to responsible sources, the rumors that the plebiscite will be postponed have no basis. The Socialist and Communist Party United Front have accused the German Front of carrying out serious terrorism and requested a postponement of the vote, which has been rejected by the Administrative Committee. In order to curb the excitement of the people and prevent accidents, the Administrative Committee issued an order today that no leaflets or newspapers may be printed or issued in the Saar tomorrow, and the sale of spirits is prohibited. Tomorrow, the sale of light wine and beer will be limited to 2:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. and 7:00 p.m. to 9:00 p.m. It is snowing heavily today, and it is expected that the hundreds of special trains carrying ballot boxes from various places and transporting voters to their places of origin to vote will be slightly delayed. Tonight, all the small mountains and the German border area will burn torches all night, and the churches will ring their bells continuously.

Now, no matter whether the German Front or the United Front gets more votes, the number of votes in favor of merging the Saar with France must be very small. The pro-France faction is scattered in various places, has no organization, and has no newspaper to carry out propaganda. It is questionable whether they can get 5,000 votes. From another point of view, the plebiscite is a very interesting event, because the people of the Saar are originally Germans, but now they can freely vote to express their opinions on Hitlerism without fear of retaliation. The National Socialist Party and the Communist Party are now paying very close attention to the plebiscite, because this move is nothing less than putting the German head of state Hitler and his comrades to the highest test, and it is also nothing less than a free election to see what direction the people's policies towards the National Socialist Party are taking. The Communist Party and the Socialists have been deeply saddened by the recent implementation of dictatorships in various European countries, which has overwhelmed their power. Therefore, in this vote, they are all in high spirits, making a final resistance.

According to a Reuters telegram from Geneva, it is expected that no major disturbances will occur during the Saar plebiscite. If serious warnings from Saarbrücken are received, an emergency meeting of the League of Nations Executive Council will be convened tomorrow night.

According to a telegram from Berlin, when the Saar plebiscite is held, all churches in Germany will ring their bells for one hour. It is reported that all churches in Germany will also pray for "justice and victory." In order to prevent messages unfavorable to Germany from spreading to the public, the German authorities have ordered the secret police to confiscate all English and French newspapers published yesterday, except for the British Times and the French Times.

Also according to news from Geneva, as soon as the results of the plebiscite are clear, the United Kingdom intends to make a concrete decision on the future of the Saar as soon as possible. It is hoped that this decision can be made at the end of this session of the League of Nations Executive Council at the end of next week. Geneva people now regard the next few days as one of the most important turning points in European history.

In recent months, the United Kingdom and France have cooperated closely on the Saar issue. Judging from the current situation, the cooperation between the two countries will continue. British Foreign Secretary Simon, Lord Privy Seal Eden, and French Foreign Minister Laval met in Geneva today for two hours, and the two sides had very harmonious opinions.

Saar Jewish residents declared today that they had received "advice" to go to Germany tonight and return after the plebiscite next week. Upon returning, they must present their passports stamped in Germany to prove that they came to participate in the vote. It is reported that this advice came from the National Socialist Party, saying that if the Saar returns to Germany, Jewish residents can avoid the revenge of punishment. (12th Reuters Dispatch)

Significance of the Saar Vote

Saarbrücken The Saar region will hold a plebiscite tomorrow. At that time, 550,000 male and female citizens of the Saar will have the right to vote. Among them, the Saar people who have joined the German Front believe that Hitler is the embodiment of Germanism, just like the previous rulers before Hitler. However, the Socialists, Communists, and some Catholics believe that the Hitler regime is actually poisoning Germany, and that the Saar region cannot be merged with Germany as long as Hitler is in power. Although the opinions of both sides are diametrically opposed, both sides recognize that the vote on January 13 is the final struggle for Germany to fight Hitler. If the pro-status quo faction wins the vote, the traditional Germanism will undoubtedly open up another path to strive for a "Fourth Germany" against Hitler. From this point of view, this Saar plebiscite has become a struggle of principle, and it should be noted by the whole world. In this plebiscite struggle, the National Socialist Party has various conveniences. The National Socialist Party engaged in large-scale propaganda, believing that those who did not vote in favor of merging with Germany betrayed Germanism and the motherland. This kind of propaganda is very effective. In addition, party members were sent to threaten residents, and those who were unwilling to blindly follow the National Socialist Party's claims would have their names put on a blacklist and punished. However, the pro-status quo faction has also achieved a great deal in recent weeks. They have tried their best to explain to the Saar people that voting in favor of maintaining the status quo at present does not mean complete separation from Germany. In the future, when the political situation in Germany changes, the Saar region can still hold a second plebiscite to merge with Germany. Therefore, there are many people in the Saar who are inclined to maintain the status quo. In addition, the Pope has repeatedly announced that the Catholic Church takes a completely neutral attitude towards the Saar vote. Therefore, Catholics will vote according to their individual will. The final outcome of tomorrow's vote is in the hands of Catholics. In short, it is currently difficult to predict the results of the vote, and it is impossible to speculate on the proportion of votes on all sides. (Havas, 12th)

British and French Foreign Ministers Hold Long Talks in Geneva

Regarding financial issues, Flandin said that those who hold securities should be able to redeem them at any time, and the government's payment of cash does not require expansion. French Prime Minister's Speech on Domestic Issues

Saving the Economic Bankruptcy

Maintaining the Republican System

(Paris) Prime Minister Flandin broadcast a speech on domestic issues today, reviewing the achievements the government has made in accordance with the cabinet's policy statement, such as passing the military budget, clarifying the wheat and wine markets, and reducing bread prices. He first said, "I only have one purpose, that is, to save France from two major disasters, namely, the economy is on the verge of bankruptcy, and the political system is in turmoil. When I formed the cabinet, it was just after the Marseille massacre. The political situation was precarious and full of dangers. When the New Year began, we saw the blue sky through the clouds and fog. Yesterday's Rome Agreement and tomorrow's London talks all have the sole purpose of consolidating peace." Flandin then described the criticisms from all sides, saying that he has a firm will to reform domestic affairs and will never be shaken. Although the industrial agreement advocated by the government has been opposed by the general public, it is actually less dangerous than the currently secretly signed industrial agreements. "I once advocated organized freedom, and I now advocate freedom of defense, because if some industries form trade associations and raise prices, the national economy will be overwhelmed, and as a result, poverty and unemployment will be created, and industrial organizations will be scattered. Economic freedom should be respected, but it should not be confused with capital's privilege over labor. Public savings should be managed by national economic institutions, but not by capitalists for profit. The government is now trying to increase loans to meet the needs of the budget and the treasury, but it should not allow the market price of issued loans to fall and the interest rate on long-term loans to rise. If not, the national economy will inevitably collapse. The government also supports reducing interest rates, because most enterprises must wait for interest rates to fall before they can resume business. As for those who hold important securities, they can redeem their securities at any time and obtain circulating funds by relying on the sound application of the discount rate and advances. If so, the same results can be achieved without implementing inflation. As for the stability of the franc, it should still be maintained. In short, the government is striving to restore trust, stimulate the people, and develop enterprises." Flandin firmly advocated that political reform should be implemented gradually. The government has submitted a judicial reform bill to Congress, stipulating that judges should be detached from politics and establish a chief inspector of judges, who will be selected from among the senior judges of the Supreme Court and the Court of Appeals, and will be responsible for managing the appointment and promotion of judges. In recent years, cases of judicial corruption have emerged one after another. Although many are fictional, public sentiment is boiling and the responsibility must be investigated. The reason why the court cannot bring all kinds of corruption cases to light is not in the corruption cases themselves, but in the way the judicial organization is structured. Now we must make judges free from political influence, and then judicial administration will be self-sufficient. The government will soon draft other political reform bills, and the House of Representatives will revise its rules of procedure. Finally, referring to foreign policy, he said that he and Foreign Minister Laval will continue the policy of peace and cooperation with all nations, saying, "I deeply know that we must be rich and strong before we can maintain peace. I will never neglect this, but I also deeply know that in international relations, we must have a spirit of compromise and practicality." Flandin also said, "I will continue to fight for the relief of unemployment and poverty, because I cannot bear to sit idly by when the common people are in deep water. I hope that the French people, regardless of political parties, will support me with good will. Egoism and pessimism are not desirable. I dare to believe that France will soon be victorious. What is the way to victory? That is, we should know to trust and not doubt, to value discipline and not scatter, to value development and not hibernate, to value action and not talk empty words." (Havas, 12th)

Germany Develops Highways

Hundreds of Thousands of People Will Participate in Road Construction

(National News Agency, Berlin) The German government recently designated 1,000 kilometers for the construction of national automobile highways. Its main purpose is to connect traffic throughout the country, making it an automobile highway network and increasing the speed of automobile travel. The groundbreaking ceremony has already been held. The German government's plan is based on the fact that automobile traffic has always been far less rapid than trains with tracks, especially automobiles traveling in the countryside. When there are vehicles carrying agricultural products, they are blocked and must travel slowly. In residential areas, we must pay attention to the safety of children and livestock on the roadside, and we cannot drive fast. Moreover, there are many curved roads, which reduces the speed of automobiles. In order to allow automobiles to travel as unimpeded as possible and to achieve a speed of 180 kilometers per hour, it is stipulated to avoid curved routes and take a straight line. At the same time, it is also required that there are no intersections with the same height on this automobile road. Where it crosses the automobile road or the railway track, tunnels or bridges are built so that the automobile can continue to move forward at its driving speed without having to wait for the wrong car. Therefore, the construction of automobiles will be similar to that of railways, with a dedicated line, with a width of seven to eight meters. In order to avoid obstructing visibility under the lights of vehicles and spotlights coming from the opposite side when driving at night, lush trees will be planted at a certain distance to absorb the reflected light. All pedestrians and any vehicles other than automobile stations are strictly prohibited from driving on automobile roads. The setting of the automobile road route should be 30 kilometers away from the busy city, and great attention is also paid to the scenery along the road. According to the Germans, hundreds of thousands of people will participate in road construction. Generally, this automobile highway is regarded as a very large artery in transportation, which will infuse new blood into the national economy. The fundamental difference between this automobile road and the railway in transportation is that travelers are not restricted by the opening hours.

American Female Aviator's Feat Flies from Honolulu to California

Eighteen Hours Across 24,000 Miles

The First Woman to Fly Across the Pacific

Oakland, California After flying from Honolulu, the famous American aviator Amelia Earhart arrived here safely in 18 hours and 16 minutes, becoming the first person to fly from Honolulu across 24,000 miles of ocean to California. Heavy fog in the Pacific slowed the flight speed slightly. Everyone was quite anxious because the scheduled time had arrived, but the woman had not yet arrived. When the woman arrived at the airfield, 5,000 people welcomed her. It is said that she felt very tired. There was still enough gasoline in the plane for several hours of flight, so there was really no need to worry about her safety. According to reports, this flight of Ms. Earhart was strongly opposed by the US Navy authorities, who were concerned about the tragedy that befell Australian aviator Ulm's recent attempt to fly between California and Honolulu. To date, ten people have lost their lives trying to navigate this route. It is also reported that Ms. Earhart is the wife of publisher Putnam. Putnam was extremely anxious after Ms. Earhart flew to Honolulu. According to William, a retired naval aviation officer who has cooperated with Ms. Earhart on several flights, Ms. Earhart did not decide on her destination before departing. Later, she decided to determine whether to go directly to Oakland or continue to Los Angeles when flying 60 miles from Oakland, depending on the motor and weather conditions of the plane. During the flight, Ms. Earhart often talked to radio stations on the West Coast via radio. Radio operators from time to time heard Ms. Earhart's "All is well" reports, her voice gentle and clear. When the plane reached the middle of the Pacific Ocean, the radio station received Ms. Earhart's report, saying that she was currently fighting against dense fog and storms. There was no news for several hours afterwards, so people here were extremely worried. But when flying 350 miles from Oakland, Ms. Earhart's "All is well" report arrived again, and then everyone felt relieved. (Reuters, 12th)

Oakland Ms. Earhart flew from Honolulu to here at 1:31 pm today, taking 19 hours and 48 minutes en route. This is the first woman to fly from Honolulu to the mainland. More than 5,000 people welcomed her. When she left the plane, the woman was in excellent spirits, wearing a flight suit, quite like Colonel Lindbergh's sister. The woman said that the weather was very good along the way, although it rained from time to time, there was no difficulty. The gasoline she carried was enough for two hours. During the flight, the woman contacted the mainland by radio from time to time. Someone asked how she felt about this trip. The woman said that although the weather was good, it was more difficult than flying across the Atlantic. According to reports, Ms. Earhart flew from Newfoundland to the United Kingdom by plane in 1923, becoming the first woman to fly across the Atlantic. Since then, she has learned to fly and has achieved great feats. The woman is Mrs. Putnam, but in public, she has called herself Ms. Earhart. (Minguo News Agency, 12th)

Belgian Government Denies Financial Crisis

Brussels The Belgian government today tried its best to deny the rumors of a financial crisis, saying that this is completely unfounded and that the treasury's cash reserves are quite sufficient, as high as 65.98%. However, according to the financial, economic and political circles, the government, because it cannot reduce the standard of living, is afraid that it will reduce the price of currency in order to increase exports. (Minguo News Agency, 12th)

Austria Continues to Try Traitors

The two were sentenced to life imprisonment and ten years imprisonment respectively for participating in the conspiracy to break into the presidential palace and force the president to sign an announcement that the government would be handed over to the Austrian Social Democratic Party. America's Great Utopia Movement (New York Correspondence)

Overcoming Economic Panic Through This

Solving the Unemployment Problem at the Same Time

After the failure of the National Industrial Recovery Act, it was followed by the "New Deal". In fact, whether this policy is effective and can save the United States from the hell of panic is still a question. Therefore, the general intellectual circles are trying to come up with ideas and methods under the current system to overcome the current economic panic. As for whether it is effective, it will be another question. Among these methods, the most eye-catching is the "American Utopian Association", originally named American Utopian Association, abbreviated as U.S.A., which is exactly the same as the abbreviation of the United States of America. Its believers believe that this is not accidental and is very helpful to the future of their movement.

The founder of the Association is "Upton L. Reed", born in Greenwich Village, Latin Quarter, New York State. This movement has now expanded considerably. Since the autumn of 1933, it has published its doctrines and held an inauguration ceremony. However, the internal organization still has some special characteristics, so it has not been fully understood, but the general outline is known to the general public. The membership fee is three US dollars and the monthly membership fee is ten cents. The membership ceremony is often held with a gathering of one or two hundred people. The participants raise their right hands and swear allegiance to the Constitution of the United States and to abide by all laws of the state, city and country. After swearing allegiance, they strive for propaganda work. The propaganda tool is a five-act play that has been compiled. The content of the Association can be seen from the plot of the play. A brief description of the plot is as follows:

The first act is set on a deep blue stage, symbolizing the social conditions of hunger and cold, and the suffering of having no money and no home. After the opening, there is a group of poorly dressed poor people. Their position in the course of life is only to beg. First, they go to a clothing store and beg the clothing store merchant to give them a few pieces of clothing to wear, but the merchant asks them for cash in exchange. They don't have a penny, so they have to endure the cold. They go to the bakery again to tell of their hunger and ask for a little bread to fill their stomachs. The shopkeeper still wants money. If they don't have money, they won't even give them bread crumbs. This group of people is wandering in hunger, and at the same time, it shows the evils of the middleman.

The second act is the high-interest lender's stage. This group of people goes to the high-interest lender to complain. The high-interest lender agrees to lend them money, but asks them for collateral. Those homeless people, what do they have to guarantee? As a result, they are at the end of their rope and have no other choice but to willingly become slaves. The stage is also hidden in semi-darkness.

In the third act, this group of vagrants is wandering aimlessly. They encounter the police, who want to accuse them as "carnivorous citizens" in accordance with the Vagrancy Law. After repeated explanations, the police seem to understand, but ask for some bribes before letting them go. Of course, they don't have money to bribe, so the police accuse them of not paying taxes. Fortunately, the judge sympathizes with the hungry workers and declares that punishing the unemployed is an unreasonable social system. Just as he is about to order their release, the high-interest lender comes out to protest and stops temporarily. This group of poor people retreats, and another rational actor comes out and says to the high-interest lender and other people, "You know that to eliminate poverty, you must replace individual selfishness with the common efforts of everyone. If so, I can lead you to a new world of common happiness."

The fourth act is set up in an ideal area. This group of poor people unknowingly arrives at this place, which is a kind of forgotten men. This is the slogan used by Roosevelt during his campaign. The rational actor explains to them the utopian polity and organization here.

The Ministry of Industry opposes the current various policies and adopts the principle of uninterrupted surplus. The Ministry of Internal Affairs is solely responsible for the supply and distribution of needs. The Ministry of Labor is responsible for production and focuses on the development of machinery. The Ministry of Education is responsible for educating people under the age of 25 and providing appropriate education according to their talents. The Ministry of National Defense advocates pan-nationalism. It only disposes of surplus items, abolishes the traditional currency system for overseas trade, and the whole United States applies a harmonious commodity exchange system for foreign trade. All nationals under the age of 25 are infants and toddlers and are in the education period. People aged 25 to 45 are productive people. People over the age of 45 have completed their production obligations and retreat from the production process. Those who do not work during the working period are treated as patients and sent to the hospital for treatment. They have no debts or credits, and there are no police agencies, but the government issues production certificates and national certificates. After the rational actor finishes speaking, the stage is hidden in darkness and the utopian song is played, urging people to become their comrades.

The fifth act is first to join the association and pay a three-dollar membership fee, and then to form a society and pass on the secret words and signals within the society.

It is said that the association already has hundreds of thousands of members, and the spread is quite fast. Can this really solve America's economic difficulties? However, it proves their ideals in difficulty. (December 15)

Deng Mingjie Discusses the Sichuan Situation and Bandit Suppression

New Provincial Government to be Established Within the Month

Bandits Have Three Major Weaknesses

Chongqing Correspondence, the Sichuan North Front, has seen no recent abnormalities. However, in the vicinity of Suiding City, Red bandits frequently harass the Sichuan army at night with guerrilla tactics. The Sichuan army is well aware of their intention to create chaos and only responds with a small number of troops. The Sichuan army was originally at Shilongxi but has now advanced to Kuzhuxi, a dozen or so miles ahead, where they are building fortifications and maintaining strict vigilance. As for the Liao and Mu troops entering Guizhou, they are currently advancing towards Meitan. Chen Mingqian's division has already departed from Fuling to the front lines. Guo Xunqi's brigade has also moved to Qinan to guard the area. The Guizhou bandits' attempt to enter Sichuan will be difficult to realize. The establishment date of the new provincial government is reportedly set for mid-month. To understand the suppression of the Red bandits and the Central Government's reforms in Sichuan, the reporter paid a special visit to Deng Mingjie, the Secretary-General of the new provincial government, yesterday, who graciously granted an interview.

Annihilation of the Remaining Bandits is Part of an Overall Plan

The reporter first inquired about the current situation of bandit suppression. According to him, the Central Government has already established an overall plan for the annihilation of the remaining bandits. All orders executed by Commander-in-Chief Liu are carried out in accordance with the Central Government's intentions. The Central Government is determined to provide the greatest support to Sichuan Province in suppressing the bandits. This sudden breakout of the remaining bandits in Jiangxi may seem rampant on the surface, but in reality, the bandits have many weaknesses and are already at the end of their rope. Their repeated attempts to avoid battle are clear evidence of this.

Bandits Have Many Weaknesses, the Three Greatest Being

Their greatest weaknesses are: (1) Most of the bandit soldiers are from Jiangxi Province. This time, their flight from Jiangxi to Guizhou was largely forced. If engaged in battle, they will inevitably collapse without being attacked. (2) Since breaking out of the encirclement last October, the bandit troops have been running through several provinces and are extremely exhausted. Moreover, the bandit masses are unable to endure the hardships of Sichuan and Guizhou, and many have expressed negativity after entering Guizhou, only unable to escape due to the strict surveillance of the bandit leaders. (3) The bandit troops lack machine guns and cannons. In normal combat, they rely solely on rifles. After suffering repeated heavy blows in Jiangxi, their ammunition is almost exhausted. This time, fleeing to Guizhou, they were pursued by eighteen divisions of the Central Army and repeatedly blocked and attacked by the armies of Hunan, Guangxi, and Guizhou, suffering heavy losses. According to current estimates, the bandit troops have no more than 20,000 guns at most. In the future, the Sichuan and Guizhou armies will join forces to suppress them, and it is certain that they can be annihilated in the short term.

Bandit Suppression and Political Reform are Equally Important

The reporter then asked about the issue of reforming Sichuan's politics. Deng replied that the Central Government has decided to carry out the reform of Sichuan's political affairs at the same time as the military suppression of the bandits. The intention is to promote military success through political power. The precedent of Jiangxi is available for reference. Deng also said that the establishment date of the new provincial government will be after the arrival of the advisory group in Sichuan. His own departure date to the province will also be around this time.

Nanchuan Builds a Chain of Pillboxes to Defend Against Communist Bandits

Furthermore, the joint defense offices of Jiangjin, Qijiang, Nanchuan, Tongzi, Suiyang, and Hejiang counties have been established, with the promotion of Instructor Ye Peilin as the director. They have also telegraphed the leaders of Sichuan and Guizhou to mobilize the joint defense forces of each county to increase defenses on the Wujiang River, in order to solidify northern Guizhou and protect southern Sichuan. In addition, the Nanchuan County government decided yesterday on three anti-communist measures: (1) Build more chain pillboxes along the border and send militiamen to patrol day and night. If an incident occurs, sound the alarm. The local military will be informed and intensify their vigilance, working together to protect the area. (2) Adopt the organizational regulations of the Anti-Communist Association, establish an office in Shuijiang Town, divide it into food and training groups, and hire military specialists to take charge, in order to strengthen border affairs. (3) Since the westward flight of the Red bandits, the number of refugees from Guizhou has been increasing daily. Special commissioners should be sent to investigate, so as to prevent wandering bandits from taking advantage of the situation and causing trouble.

Confession of Wang Guangze, Commander of the Pseudo-Independent Division

A General Overview of Xiao’s Bandit Strength

The Passage from Jiangxi to Sichuan

Chongqing Correspondence, the Longtan garrison, Tian Guanwu Brigade, recently captured Wang Guangze, commander of the Red bandit pseudo-Sixth Army Corps Independent Division, along with his chief of staff Wu Jinshan, political commissar Cong Chuantong, political director Wei Xiaofen, security bureau chief Liu Daidan, and other leaders, as well as more than 300 bandit officers and soldiers. They have repeatedly presented them to Commander-in-Chief Liu and forwarded them to Chairman Jiang of the Military Affairs Commission for instructions on how to handle them. It is now learned that Wang's bandit, while detained in Tian Brigade headquarters, recounted his entry into the bandit ranks and the real situation of the bandit troops. The record is as follows:

"I (Wang Guangze referred to himself below) am from Hengshan County, Hunan Province, and I am 32 years old. I have four brothers, and my family is doing well. I do business selling wood, hides, cattle and sheep, and also cultivate my own fields. In the eighth year of the Republic of China, I joined the army under Peng, the brigade commander of the First Brigade of Zhang Jingyao's army. After a year, I was promoted to sergeant. In the tenth year of the Republic of China, I became a platoon leader. Three months later, because the troops returned to Shanxi, I asked for leave to go home and do business. In the eighteenth year, I joined the army under Wang Pi, the First Division of Wu Shang's Eighth Army. Soon after, I became a private, then a platoon leader. In May of the nineteenth year, I opened up Jiangxi from Hunan to fight Zhu De. After three pursuits and suppressions, I fought to Jinggang Mountain in December. Later, Wu's army was transferred back to Hunan and stationed in You County for reorganization. The army was reduced to a division, and the division was reduced to a regiment. At that time, I was a platoon leader in the Ninth Company of the Third Battalion of the First Regiment. The Ninth Company was disbanded, and everyone was unwilling to continue. I went home again to do business, selling wood and hides to Chaling. I met the Red Army and was arrested. All the capital I had with me, more than 1,700 yuan, was robbed. They persuaded me to work for them. At that time, I couldn't distinguish the good from the bad of the Red Army. I thought it was the same as the ordinary government army, and I could hope for some future, so I joined the Red Army. After joining, because I was a soldier and understood some military common sense, they sent me to Yaobi Chang, Chaling, as the captain of the Red Guard Battalion, with a number of more than 120, all with knives and sticks, with no good guns. When I was the captain of the battalion, they asked me to do whatever they wanted, and I worked very hard. Until September 1931 (that is, the twentieth year of the Republic of China), the Chaling County Soviet transferred me to be the company commander of the guard company. Soon after, I was promoted to the captain of the guerrilla battalion, with three companies under my command, each company with about 30 guns. The role of the guerrillas was to specifically disrupt the government army's line of battle and threaten the rear. I put a lot of effort into it. Afterwards, I was transferred to be the battalion commander of the independent battalion of the Xianggan Provincial Military Region in the Red District. Xianggan Province refers to the border area between Jiangxi and Hunan provinces, including Chaling, You County, Ling County, Zixing, and other counties in Hunan, and Yongxin, Ninggang, Lianhua, Ji'an, Wan'an, Taihe, Anfu, and other counties in Jiangxi, with Yongxin as the center. The provincial committee organization is located in that area. The military region commander is Cai Huiwen. The independent battalion has three companies, three machine guns, and each company has a machine gun platoon, with one machine gun. I was the independent battalion. Three months later, I fought several battles with Wang Dongyuan, Li Jue, Chen Guangzhong, Peng Weiren, and other divisions. The Hunan army suffered great losses. After these battles, my independent battalion was expanded into an independent regiment. At that time, the organization of the Red Army in Xianggan Province had 24 divisions. The division commander was Long Ling. There was a replenishment division, a first division, the division commander was Tian Haiqing, an eighth division, an independent regiment, a total of more than 20,000 rifles, 140 machine guns, and 36 mortars. Xiao Ke was the 18th division sent by Mao Zedong from the Central Government in 1933 (that is, the 22nd year of the Republic of China) with more than 1,000 people and guns to be compiled into the Sixth Army Corps. Cai Huiwen was dismissed. In January of this year, my independent regiment was changed to the 53rd Regiment. In June, I departed from Yongxin. An independent division, three independent regiments, and five independent battalions were still left in the Xianggan area. The main force all fled westward. At that time, the team was reorganized into the pseudo-Sixth Army Corps Commander Xiao Ke, the pseudo-Seventeenth Division Commander Xiao Ke concurrently, the pseudo-Eighteenth Division Commander Long Ling, the pseudo-Military Camp School, and the pseudo-Army Corps. After departing from Xianggan, passing through the border between Guangdong and Guangxi, arriving at , Xiao Ke announced an order, saying, "In order to disrupt the enemy and contain the people, so that the pseudo-central retreat cancels the government army, the first step of the plan has now been completed, and the second step of the plan must be implemented quickly." At that time, what was the first step of the plan, and what was the second step of the plan, Ding Jin did not announce to us, so we continued to advance from Chengbu, to receive the task of passing through. In the battle of Wencun on the border between Hunan and Guizhou, I lost more than 100 people. When I arrived in Xiajiang, Guizhou, I prepared to rest for a day. I met the joint encirclement of the Hunan and Guangxi armies and pursued them, losing a battalion of the 52nd Regiment and a battalion of the 54th Regiment. I fought with the 53rd Regiment, still covering the passage of the entire army corps. In Chengbu, I fought with Li Jue's troops, and my right leg was injured. When I arrived in Huangping, Guizhou, Xiao Ke and Ren Bishi announced the pseudo-central order, saying, "Our task is to join forces with He Long, and develop a Red District in Xiang, E, Chuan, and Qian. If we are blocked and dispersed by the government army, we will disintegrate and gather in the direction of Yinjiang, and then find He Long." We fought with the Guangxi army in Qingxi. A battalion of the 49th Regiment and two battalions of the 51st Regiment, a total of three battalions, were cut off. The political commissar of the 17th Division, Li Da, led a fierce charge forward. When he arrived at Fengxiangxi, he had lost two-thirds of his men before he could approach He Long. He Long reported to Li, and he knew that Xiao had arrived and sent troops to meet him, and he met with him at a distance of about 40 li between Benhuang and Ganlongkou. The next day, he arrived at Nan Yaojie. Xiao's troops had 12,000 people when they departed, but only 6,000 or 7,000 people gathered at this time, with 3,000 casualties and 2,000 escaped. Xiao had two radio transceivers, one large and one small. The large one had a power-driven motor. The small one used dry batteries. After camping every day, he telegraphed the pseudo-central government. A senior meeting was held in Nan Yaojie. The attendees included Ren Bishi, Chairman of the Red Sixth Army Corps specially sent by the pseudo-central government (a student studying in Russia), Li Bu, Secretary-General of the Political Department of the pseudo-Army Corps (a student studying in Russia), Gan Shiqi, Political Commissar of the pseudo-18th Division (a student studying in Russia), as well as Xiao Ke, He Long, Guan Xiangyin, Wang Zhen, Liu Shiji, Fang Liming, Xia Xi, and other important senior personnel. First, Xia Xi reported on the actions of the Red Second Army Corps (ie, He Long's troops, formerly known as the Red Third Army, now renamed the Second Army Corps) after Honghu. Then, everyone pointed out Xia's mistakes. The public decided to remove Xia from his post and immediately telegraphed the pseudo-central government for approval. Since then, all the power of the Second and Sixth Army Corps has been in the hands of Ren Bishi alone. Xia Xi also reported that there was a Red District organization with a width of more than 100 li in Fengxiangxi, with 800 people in the Qiandong Independent Regiment, more than 500 people in the Deyi Independent Regiment, and the Sixth Army Corps allocated six machine guns, a company of pistols, and two battalions of infantry to my command. There were also two guerrilla teams and the remaining wounded and sick soldiers. During the meeting, I was appointed as the commander of the Qiandong Soviet Area Combat District Command, and it was agreed to send transportation twice a month to find the team in the direction of Youyang Xiushan to make contact. The next day, they went to Youyang, and I went to Fengxiangxi, and planned to reorganize the team into three regiments. The first regiment was led by Regiment Commander Qin, the second regiment was led by Regiment Commander Tang, and the third regiment was led by Regiment Commander Wu. Xiao Ke sent an order on the way, calling me to be compiled into an independent division. In Fengxiangxi, I was greatly oppressed by the Guizhou army, and after several fierce battles, I suffered great losses and could not gain a foothold. I planned to flee to Fanjingshan to defend it, but the work in the mountains had not yet been completed, and the Guizhou army attacked and occupied it again. So I fled from Zhaiying to Yimei, and wanted to flee from Yimei to western Hunan to join Xiao He. However, I was ambushed by the Miao people in front of Yimei, and lost most of them. In Pingma Yongdong Shangchuan, the troops were blocked by the army and the local defense along the way. The troops have been completely disarmed, and the machine guns and pistols have also been disarmed. I was about to escape, but I was surrounded and captured by your army. I only read books for three years before. After joining the Red Army, I had been to the Red Army Training Team and the Red Army School, and I had graduated. Because I was short-sighted, I mistakenly entered the wrong path. This is a period of my experience in the Red Army. I am very grateful to Brigade Commander Tian for his preferential treatment. It allows me to be instructed here, to understand the great righteousness, and deeply regret my past mistakes. I am determined to oppose communism. In the future, I should seek to perform sincerely in my work. The Red Army is cruel and inhuman, and it is difficult to exist for a long time, and it must be eliminated." According to reports, after Wang's bandit was captured, Liu Xiang had approved the military and local affairs bureau to execute Wang's bandit on the spot.

A Japanese Ship Hits and Sinks a Customs Patrol Boat in Wuhu

Customs Officers Fall into the Water and are Rescued

Japanese Consul Negotiates Release

Caihu Correspondence, Anhui Province has a very abundant fish production in the upper reaches, with annual sales to Nanjing, Shanghai, Zhenjiang, and Tongzhou worth tens of thousands of yuan. Because there are no customs posts in the interior, most of them are transported to Wuhu from Datong Anqing by civilian ships first, and then declared for export by Wuhu Customs. However, Wuhu Customs has recently found that fish merchants often smuggle and evade taxes, so they are very strict in their inspection of Jianglun boats passing through Wuhu. Yesterday, the Japanese merchant ship Luoyang Maru was launched. Due to heavy fog, it was delayed until 2:00 PM before arriving at the Wuhu Wharf. Wuhu Customs received a report that a lot of private fish was being smuggled, so they sent Customs officers Chen and Qian to board the ship for inspection. Unexpectedly, before the inspection was completed and the two customs officers had not left the ship, the Luoyang Maru suddenly drummed its wheels, left the wharf, and sailed downstream. Seeing this situation, Wuhu Customs immediately sent two more customs officers to track it down on the customs' Anhui Electric, a small gasoline patrol boat. At that time, the Luoyang Maru had already sailed to the middle of the river, and the water was turbulent, and the waves were surging, causing the Anhui Electric patrol boat to be hit and sunk by the Luoyang Maru. Fortunately, the two customs officers had already climbed onto the Luoyang Maru, and the two people who fell into the water, Lao Da Huang Xueqing and Lao Gui Lei Youbao, were also rescued by boatmen, avoiding a tragedy. Seeing that an accident had occurred, Wuhu Customs used flag signals to stop the Luoyang Maru from sailing. Later, the Japanese Consul in Wuhu, Takeyoshi Sadaharu, rushed to Wuhu Customs and contacted the tax department. The Luoyang Maru did not start sailing downstream until 4:30. Wuhu Customs has decided to investigate the matter strictly in accordance with the law. (11th)

Banditry in Anhui is Almost Completely Eliminated

Liu Zhenhua Establishes a Reception Center in Yanghu Town

Anhui Provincial Government Distributes 3,500 Stones of Relief Rice

Wuhu Correspondence, Luo Binghui's bandit troops, the pseudo-Nineteenth Division Commander Xun Weizhou (formerly the pseudo-Seventh Army Corps Commander), under the command of the bandit leader Zhu De, used the false name of the Northern Anti-Japanese Advance Team to sneak into southern Anhui, intending to occupy the deep mountains of Huizhou as a nest, create a Red District, and join forces with Fang Zhimin in Tangkou, reorganized into the pseudo-Tenth Army Corps, with a temporary total of more than 6,000 people. However, they did not know that today's southern Anhui is not comparable to the Jiangxi of the past. The self-defense force is relatively sufficient, and the residents have not been seduced by the bandits, and the national army has always followed up and suppressed them, and the bandits have lost the opportunity to establish a nest. They fled east and west, and their strength has gradually disappeared. In addition, after each battle, there are many who suddenly woke up and surrendered. The Anhui Provincial Government Chairman's Office in Tunxi recently learned from the surrendered pseudo-Minister of Health Hu Yungeng, platoon leader Chen Daonan, and bandit soldiers that the number of bandits is now less than 3,000, and the number of guns is only one-third. Many senior bandit officers were also injured or killed. For example, a certain Zhou, the director of the pseudo-Security Bureau, Xi Miyu, the chief of staff, Yue Shaohua, the political commissar, and Liu Ying, the political director, were all seriously injured in Fenshui, Zhangjiajing, and Tanjiaqiao. It is reported that the Xun bandit Weizhou died in Maolin Village, Jing County, after being wounded in Tanjiaqiao. Now, the bandit cadres and soldiers below the regimental commander are very shaken. During each mobile operation, 30 to 40 people flee every day. Liu Zhenhua believes that many of the fleeing responsible members of the pseudo-agency are willing to surrender and reform and participate in anti-communism, and they can also fully describe the pseudo-organization, which shows that they are mostly due to economic oppression, ignorance, blind obedience, or being coerced, so he followed the Nanchang Camp's promulgated method of recruiting and pacifying surrenders and dealing with prisoners, and established a reception center in Yanghu Town on the opposite bank of Tunxi. There are considerable facilities for clothing, food, and housing, and Chen Xiaobo has been appointed as the director, He Qiming as the administrator, and Liu Yizhi as the trainer, to give them training and influence, or send them back to their hometowns separately, in order to open up a new path. In the past, when the counties of Huizhou and Shexian were raided by bandits, many people fled one after another, displaced, fathers and sons were not protected, and husbands and wives did not care for each other, which was extremely miserable. Now the bandits have been almost completely eliminated, and the military strength of each county is strong and the defense is solid, which can ensure that there will be no future troubles. They have all issued notices to gather people back to their hometowns to seek proper resettlement, and the provincial government has decided to distribute 3,500 stones of relief rice to Huizhou for relief. However, because the transportation costs require nearly 10,000 yuan, Liu Jianzhong, the commissioner of the area, has sent separate letters to wealthy fellow villagers from Huizhou living abroad to persuade them to donate money to raise funds for transportation. In addition, after the Huizhou bandits were surrounded and chased, a small number of remnants fled to Shidai Taiping Qidu and other places. The majority of the □□□ division has taken the road to Qidu, stationed in Jiaocun, Taiping, and dispatched teams to build pillboxes in the key points of Shidai Taiping Qingyang and other counties. There are also many pillboxes built from Nanyangwan north through Jiuhua Mountain to Miaoqian, which are very dense and tight. The remaining bandits will soon be caught. (11th)

Henan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi Rural Cooperation Conference

The Conference is Expected to Last Three or Four Days

Nanchang Correspondence, bandit disasters have spread in Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, and other provinces for seven or eight years, and bankrupt rural areas have been destroyed without any remainder. In addition to carrying out agricultural relief and immigration and reclamation, the Nanchang Camp and the general headquarters of the three provinces for bandit suppression believe that the only way to restore the rural economy is to promote cooperation. When Chairman Jiang supervised and suppressed the Red bandits in the three provinces, he promulgated the articles of association of the rural cooperative preparatory society, and tried them out in the recovered areas of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi. Since the various places in this province have been recovered successively, the camp also instructed the Jiangxi Rural Cooperation Committee to act as a rural relief area in each newly recovered area and semi-bandit area, to handle credit, utilization, and sales cooperation of various kinds, and to purchase plowing cattle, seeds, and agricultural implements for the victims of the disaster. Now, the cooperation associations of the four provinces believe that the remaining bandits will soon be eliminated and rural construction will begin. In order to intensify their work to seek universality, they are holding a discussion meeting on rural cooperation work in the four provinces in Nanchang. The meeting place is located in the conference hall of the Jiangxi Rural Cooperation Association on the shore of Donghu Lake in this city. It opened at 9:00 AM on the 7th. Those who attended were Wu Jing, director of the Henan Cooperation Association, Xu Qinglan, chief inspector, Liu Renqiu, chief inspector of Hubei, Yang Xingcun, director of the Anhui, Zheng Dasheng, chief inspector, Xiong Zaiwei, director of the Jiangxi, Yang Yunfu, chief inspector, Li Anlu, design specialist, Zou Huagai, relief director, Li Yuji, Hu Jian, Zhou Guocai, and Wei Jingchu and Du Keming, directors of the Jiangxi office of the Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Association, and more than ten others. Wen Qun, director of the camp's cooperation team and chairman of the Jiangxi Cooperation Committee, presided over the meeting and delivered a speech, saying, "Rural cooperation is the main task for the recovery of rural areas and the development of production. All four provinces have started to implement it. Regarding the various laws, regulations, plans, and work implementation, the colleagues of the four provinces should explore and correct each other based on practical experience." Then, the representatives of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi reported on the work of their respective provinces in turn, and nominated members of each group's review committee to submit proposals for review. The meeting is expected to last for three or four days. (9th)

Military Police in Shantou Strictly Suppress the People's Postal Service

Search Pedestrians in Streets and Alleys

Shantou Correspondence, the Ministry of Transportation has ordered the military and political authorities of various provinces to cooperate with the post office to suppress the people's postal service and to limit the people's postal service in all places to end uniformly at the end of the 23rd year of the Republic of China. This order is being carried out vigorously. There were originally 18 people's postal service offices in Shantou, specializing in collecting and sending letters to Hong Kong, Shanghai, Hankou, Xiamen, Fuzhou, and the inland areas of Chao and Jie. Delivery has always been known for its speed and reliability. Since the ministry's order was announced to cancel it, the Guangdong Provincial Government also issued orders to the public security bureaus of each county and city government, ordering the stationed troops and police to cooperate with the postal bureau to execute it. December 31 was the last day for the people's postal service to end. Ordinary letters can still be sent by parcel, but the post office has resolutely revoked the business licenses of the people's postal service. At that time, the Shantou People's Postal Service Association issued a declaration requesting assistance from all walks of life. The Shantou Silver Industry Association believed that obstacles would occur in the remittance and delivery of drafts in the future, so it held a meeting on New Year's Day to discuss the matter and discuss reliable and fast methods of delivery in the future. The Shantou Chamber of Commerce also wrote to the Municipal Government Public Security Bureau regarding this matter, requesting a postponement of the execution of the ban, because there were millions of yuan of drafts every day at the end of the lunar year. After this presentation, there was no reply. The most relevant thing is the letters from overseas Chinese in Singapore, Siam, Hong Kong, and other places. Because overseas Chinese remit silver back to their hometowns, the letter must accompany the silver, and then it can be delivered to poor and remote villages in each county. Now that the people's postal service has been banned, it cannot be sent in bulk packages. Batch letters must be affixed with stamps and sent separately. Problems will arise in the future delivery of silver, return of batch letters, etc. It is heard that the post office still allows the batch postal service to be packaged, and the letters must be affixed with sufficient stamps. The amount of silver must be written on the letter. If the letter only says that a certain treasure number is received, it will be considered a normal letter mixed in and will inevitably be opened and read. In addition, the Shantou military police party and government agencies originally sent several members of the mail inspection committee. The situation is serious, so more people have been added. Now, batch letters are also subject to strict inspection. The delivery of batch letters will inevitably be delayed. It is impossible to destroy it even if people do not want to destroy it. Starting from New Year's Day, the military police in Shantou suppressed private letters with very strict arrangements. The customs fronts of each embankment wharf, Chenghai bus station, and Qiluwei are lined with military police. Reconnaissance teams, inspectors, special service teams, and patrol police can search the bodies of pedestrians everywhere to see if there are any private letters. The post office also notified various merchants, stating that the people's postal service has been cancelled. If anyone is found to have given the letter to someone for private delivery, they will be severely fined. There is also an official document to the Hong Kong post office. If a person carrying private letters is captured in Hong Kong, they should be sent back to Shantou for serious punishment. Under this situation, it is credible that no private letter can fly out in the Chaoshan area. From now on, the work of mail inspectors will inevitably become busier. (5th)

The Complete Elimination of Remaining Bandits in Northeastern Fujian is Imminent

Scattered Bandits Along the Min River Have Been Eliminated

Fuzhou Dispatch: After the recapture of the bandit areas in northern Fujian, there remained a remnant of about two thousand bandits, entrenched in the areas of Quanshang, Wucun, Fengxi, Bangang, Junkou, and Tangdi in Ninghua County. They constructed defensive fortifications and established a bogus "Min-Gan Military Region Command" in an attempt to revive their activities. Lu Xingrong, commander of the 52nd Division, led his troops to suppress them, recovering Quanshang, Wucun, and Fengxi one by one. Recently, the 33rd Regiment of the Lu Division advanced from Fengxi to attack Tangdi, encountering over a thousand bandits, including the bogus 118th and 120th Regiments, as well as the Training Corps and Guard Company. After a day-long fierce battle, they killed the bogus Command's Chief of Staff, Jiang Han, the Political Director, Peng Hu, and over two hundred bandit soldiers, seizing over one hundred rifles. The bogus Commander, Song Chengquan, and the Political Commissar, Lai Chang, led their remaining forces to flee towards Bangang and Junkou. The Lu Division is currently in pursuit. Furthermore, four bandit groups, led by Weng Shousong, Chen Jiansheng, Lu Chengguang, and Wei Jiankang, numbering about six hundred in total, have been causing disturbances along the Yanping (present-day Nanping) Xiafuzhou and Shangmin River areas. They specialize in extorting "donations" from upstream boats and downstream timber rafts, often killing raft workers and robbing passengers, causing great distress to travelers. Recently, the Security Team's Special Operations Regiment has been conducting encirclement operations in areas such as Shuikou and Huangyou Bay, scattering the Lu Chengguang and Wei Jiankang groups. The remaining bandits have fled to the borders of Yanping and Jian'ou counties. The Weng Shousong and Chen Jiansheng groups, totaling three hundred men, along with their weapons, were all captured and transported to the provincial capital for detention in the Security Office a few days ago. The Min River shipping route should now be safe and stable. As for the remaining Red bandits in eastern Fujian, they have been driven to exhaustion after being rigorously suppressed by the National Army. However, sporadic bandit groups still appear near Shekou in Fu'an County. Chen Zheng, the commander of the 1st Regiment of the New 10th Division stationed in the county, recently led two battalions of his troops on patrols in various areas. The bandit activity has now been suppressed, but the bandits in Fuding County are still concentrated in the Taimu Mountain area and are quite rampant. The security team stationed in the county has also advanced from Bailin to suppress them, engaging in fierce battles with the bandits.

Warning Letter Causes Elderly Man's Sudden Death in Songjiang

Cao Fangqing, a merchant over fifty years old, was responsible for buying and selling rice at the Shengji Rice Shop in the West Beach for many years. Several days ago, his demeanor suddenly changed, and his spirits were low. After being questioned by his employer, it was revealed that he had received a warning letter from Yao Zhang, the mother of his daughter-in-law. The letter stated that her daughter had been married for three years and, although the couple's feelings were still good, she could not bear the abuse from her mother-in-law, so she had returned home in Ningbo and was studying at an adult women's school. The letter then listed various conditions, set a three-day deadline for a response, and requested that the reply be delivered to a Mr. Yang. Upon receiving the letter, Cao Fangqing became worried, anxious, and frightened, leading to an altered state. On the afternoon of the 12th, at 3:00 PM, when the warning period expired, Cao Fangqing's expression suddenly changed, and he died shortly after. Upon questioning his daughters-in-law, they claimed to be unaware of the situation, asserting that Mr. Yang was instigating the situation, inciting the ignorant Yao Zhang to resort to such measures. The Cao family is extremely indignant and will be lodging a complaint against the Yang family.

"Jian" of Nantong's Ji'an Steamer Strikes a Dyke at Yaogang

The Taikoo Company's Ji'an steamer ran aground in heavy fog at Yaogang at 4:00 AM on the 11th while sailing downstream to Tongzhou. The ship collided heavily with a breakwater embankment, breaking in two and sinking. Fortunately, the ship ran aground in shallow water, and the crew, passengers, and cargo were safely unloaded. The shipowner immediately telegraphed the company, dispatching employees to Tongzhou to handle the aftermath.

County to Implement Baojia System in Stages

The Nantong County Baojia system has now been compiled, and the county government has ordered all districts to implement it in stages: (1) This month, implement guard duty, security patrols, sanitation management, and investigation of opium and drugs; (2) Starting in February, collect labor for dredging rivers, building roads, and afforestation; (3) Starting in March, promote rural sideline industries and various investigations, and promote social education.

The Reestablishment of Suzhou's General Labor Union

The Suzhou General Labor Union, which was disbanded by order three years ago, is now being reestablished under the instruction of the Central People's Movement Committee. The County Party Committee convened a meeting of representatives from various industry labor unions yesterday afternoon to elect preparatory committee members. Xia Xuejun was publicly elected as chairman, and Shen Changqing, Xia Xuejun, Lu Jupo, Wang Suijia, and Wu Baoshu were elected as preparatory committee members. The first preparatory committee meeting was then held, chaired by Xia Xuejun. It was decided to divide the committee into four sections: General Affairs, Organization, Training, and Propaganda, and directors were appointed for each section. The County Party Committee building was used as the office, and Wang Suijia was assigned to receive files and objects and to carry out preparatory work.

Change in Head of Business Tax Bureau

Bao Gongchao, head of the Wu County Business Tax Bureau, has been ordered to transfer to the province and await further assignment. His vacancy will be filled by Guo Shibai. After receiving the appointment, Guo arrived in Suzhou yesterday and is scheduled to take office on the 16th.

Wuxi Thugs Impersonating Officials Arrested for Extortion

Ni Ronggen, a well-known soil merchant from Xiaosanliqiao outside the North Gate of this county, was arrested by the Supervisory Office on July 9th last year. Over one hundred and forty taels of various opium dross and paste were seized, and he was sent to the court and sentenced to imprisonment. His wife, tempted by the high profits, continued to trade in opium, with thriving business. At 10:00 AM on the 9th of this month, two thugs, Yan A'da and Wang Fenglin, ordered the old woman Wang Xie, with three silver dollars and sixty copper coins, to buy an ounce of opium from the Ni family. At the same time, they led accomplices Wang Yiting and Yang Yongtai, claiming to be secret agents from the Supervisory Office, to search the premises. As a result, forty silver dollars (or four hundred, according to another account) were extorted, with thirty dollars still outstanding. When leaving, they were seen by another thug, Zhang Aisheng. Fearing exposure, they gave Zhang two silver dollars as hush money. The next day, Wang, the chief inspector, was secretly informed and arrested Gu A'da, Yang Yongtai, Wang Yiting, Zhang Aisheng, and Wang Xie, sending them to the Public Security Bureau and then to the local court for investigation and prosecution.

Zhenjiang to Improve Public Security Facilities in Various Counties

In order to standardize and improve public security facilities in various counties, the Jiangsu Civil Affairs Department has decided to convene meetings of public security administrative personnel from various counties in stages, starting on February 20th of this year, to discuss ways to improve public security. Counties with bureaus will be represented by the head of the county bureau or the director or section chief of the directly affiliated public security section. Each will prepare a report and proposal on the state of public security facilities in their county and submit them to the department by the end of the month for discussion at the meeting. The department has drafted the dates for the staged meetings, the reporting items, and the scope of the proposals, and has issued orders to the county magistrates to inform them to comply and to report to the department in advance.

First Batch of Small Loans Approved

The Jiangsu Provincial Small Loan Office for Common People began issuing loans on the 5th. Approximately three to four thousand small business owners applied for loans, with a total loan amount of over forty thousand yuan. After review, only forty-four households were qualified. Based on the actual need for funds, the amounts were appropriately reduced, totaling over one thousand three hundred yuan, with the largest being two hundred yuan and the smallest being three yuan. Each household has been notified to complete loan papers and collect the funds.

Changshu's Fourth District Famine Victims Riot Again

Due to the severe drought last summer, the harvest in the county's various townships was drastically reduced. Some farmers, plagued by hunger and cold, have repeatedly launched famine riots. Fortunately, in the sixth district, the Party and government were able to suppress the situation, bringing it to an end. Unexpectedly, the fourth district in the west, due to negligence in inspection during the disaster assessment, was not listed as a severely affected area. However, the Yuluba area indeed had no harvest. On the 5th of this month, a famine riot occurred once. As a result, three or four hundred hungry men and women were each given ten copper coins and dispersed. Then, on the 11th, District Chief Xu Jingyu and others went to Zhoujia Wharf to compile and inspect the Baojia system. Villagers beat drums and gathered a crowd, assembling over three hundred people in a short time, demanding the exemption of rent and seeds and the distribution of winter relief. District Chief Xu promised to find a solution and immediately returned. However, the famine victims were dissatisfied and continued to go to the district office, demanding a responsible response. The district chief had not yet returned, so Assistant Zhao persuaded them. Fearing trouble, he urgently telegraphed the port Public Security Bureau to dispatch police to suppress them. Bureau Chief Cheng Jingchuan immediately rushed to the scene on horseback, but due to muddy roads, soaked from prolonged rains, he fell from his horse into the field and was seriously injured. At the district office in Xitangqiao, the district assistant ordered the farmers of each township to sign their names, awaiting submission to the county government to request winter relief. The famine victims signed the agreement, and were given six copper coins each before they dispersed.

Yangzhou: City and Rural Opium Dens Draw Lots Again

The Jiangdu County Opium Prohibition Committee, after approval from the provincial capital, submitted to the seventh meeting the decision to add twenty opium dens in the urban area and to supplement the rural areas with fewer than five dens to have five each. Opium Prohibition Committee members Zhou Guren, Dai Tianqiu, Zhang Shu, Dong Chengqi, and Committee Chairman Ma Zhenbang, License Section Chief Chang Shizhi, Yin Muguo, and others were present. There were fourteen applicants in the rural areas, with Luo Maoxun of Daqiao, Qirui Lin of Zhongzha in District Five; Zhang Zhan'ao and Zheng Kun of Yiling in District Six; Qian Run of Dayi in District Eight; Zhou Zhongming of Wang Jueqiao and Gu Hong of Yangjia Miao, and You Licheng of Tuzi Qiao in District Nine (all drawn by County Magistrate Ma). Those who won the lot were instructed to promptly report for business, while those who did not win could retrieve their previously paid deposits with the receipts issued at the time of application. It was also announced that Hu Min, a member of the committee, was impersonating and extorting six yuan per month from opium dens in the eastern countryside and has now fled. Anyone encountering similar cases of extortion should immediately report to the county government. Section Chief Chang then instructed those who won the lot in the rural areas to follow the procedures to obtain a license and start business within three days before dispersing.

Shanghai Public Security Bureau Advises Private Letter Offices to Suspend Operations

Private Letter Offices Held a Meeting Yesterday to Assist Baoshun Private Letter Office

Dagon News Agency reports that the private letters sent from the main Private Letter Offices of Shanghai and other places to Wenzhou have been missing, and the Shanghai Public Security Bureau has advised the Private Letter Offices to suspend operations again. The National Private Letter Businessmen held a general representative meeting yesterday to discuss methods to assist the Baoshun Private Letter Office and other matters. The details are as follows:

Missing Private Letters Sent to Wenzhou

Seven Private Letter Offices in this port, including Zhengda and Quansheng, have been specializing in private letters between Shanghai and Wenzhou. Since December 31st of this year, the last batch of private letters sent from Shanghai to Wenzhou have been missing, and the Wenzhou Private Letter Offices have not received any of them. The senders in Shanghai have been asking the Private Letter Offices, etc., and it has been more than ten days, but the whereabouts are still unknown and is being investigated.

The Municipal Public Security Bureau Advises to Stop Business Again

The Municipal Public Security Bureau stated that most of the Private Letter Offices are located in Nanshi Xian Gua Street, within the jurisdiction of the police. In accordance with the central government's orders, it had previously sent personnel to advise them. Now that the deadline has passed, the offices are still operating as usual, which seems to violate the law. The Public Security Bureau of the 16th Division was instructed to implement it again, so the division specially summoned the representative of Yinyuantong on the afternoon of the previous day and advised them to end their operations on the same day and remove the signs of all the Private Letter Offices. The letter offices requested a postponement because the central government has not yet approved the petition order.

Letter Offices from All Over Held a Meeting Yesterday

The National Private Letter Offices have repeatedly petitioned the central government, but there has been no reply on whether to ban them or not. However, the post office has abolished the weighing regulations, and from January 1st of this year, if private letters are found again, they will be detained and punished. The letter offices are deeply panicked, so they held a general representative meeting yesterday afternoon to discuss the final petition for relief, and attached the First Special District Court's verdict on the Baoshun Private Letter Office incident and decided to appeal.
