Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 7: Hearing the Words, She Covers Her Face and Weeps as She Sells Herself, Liu Xin Seeks to Probe, Please East, Pious Hope

Li Shilian had seen these things with his own eyes. At this time, it would be unreasonable to keep urging Yueying to speak. But if he let her go, he would have no way to answer Jia Duocai. As he thought about this, he first stood up abruptly, then slowly sat down. But before his buttocks were firmly seated, he stood up again. Amidst his unstable state, Cheng Zhiqian understood early on and laughed: "Mr. Li seems to intend to find this girl as his concubine. You can proceed, it will not be hindered in any way because of me." Li Shilian laughed: "Mr. Cheng, do you see how we are almost having trouble even eating two meals? How can we still be happy? It is this Mr. Jia in front, I don't know how, who has taken a fancy to this girl and wants to get her." Cheng Zhiqian said lightly: "So, this girl's body already has a patron." Li Shilian said: "This Mr. Jia is my friend, a very good person. His intention is also to feel that this girl is very pitiful. Taking her would be saving her." Zhiqian said: "This gentleman is surnamed Jia, oh, Jia of Jia Baoyu, haha! No wonder he is so amorous." Li Shilian felt that such mocking words were inappropriate. One is willing to be a concubine, and one is willing to marry a concubine. Why are onlookers saying such nonsense? As he pondered in his heart, he also wanted to retaliate with a few words, but in the space of his thoughts, the waiter brought up a dinner invitation, as well as a notice written on red paper. Zhiqian took the invitation, threw it on the table first, and laughed: "Why are we invited again?" Only then did he look at the notice. Li Shilian's seat was not far from the table. The folded invitation was opened upwards. Looking intently, he saw that it was written "Respectfully Ordered by Gao Hesheng." Gao Hesheng was the director of the Construction Department, unexpectedly Cheng Zhiqian also knew him. To say that he was a semi-rich man in Xi'an was no exaggeration. He wanted to make inroads into the construction field, so this was someone he should contact. (111)

The Origin of the Red Hats Worn by Street Cleaners

— Lu Wu

In Shanghai, on every street, we can see street cleaners wearing red hats and red vests, working very carefully, sweeping up the debris on the streets and the fruit peels and scraps of paper that people unintentionally discard.

Why do they have to wear red hats?

In 1792, during the height of the French Revolution, some of King Louis XVI's loyal guards, seeing the tense revolutionary mood of the people of Paris at that time, also rebelled and secretly ran to the side of the people's revolutionary army to help with the revolutionary work.

However, some of the rebellious soldiers were caught by the non-rebellious guards, who sent them to places with many people to do hard labor, and made them wear red hats. Their intention was: on the one hand, to prevent them from escaping, as the red hats would really attract a lot of attention.

This was a form of punishment and extreme humiliation.

At that time, the revolutionary people of Paris, seeing that the revolutionary comrades standing on the same front as themselves were subjected to such great humiliation and pain, expressed great sympathy. However, for a moment, they couldn't think of any good way to help them get rid of this shame. Later, everyone simply wore red hats to confuse the sight of the guards, making it difficult for them to see who the arrested soldiers were. Soon, many inexplicable people also wore red hats to show off, and later, more and more people wore them. The red hat actually became a symbol of revolutionary elements.

However, the red hat, which was misunderstood as a symbol of the spirit of revolutionary elements, in present-day Shanghai, has returned to the original label of being punished to do hard labor! You see, now, not only street cleaners wear red hats, but also porters at train stations, workers on docks... which coolie is not wearing a red hat?

Tidbits

— (Yan Xinquan)

Ms. SS is a staunch advocate of celibacy. But there are more than a dozen men chasing her, which I find a bit strange. Later, according to someone in the know: "Although she strongly advocates celibacy, it proves that she is currently alone. It can be said that it is a countermeasure of hers, giving us a way in. When she has a partner, don't worry that she won't shout that love is sacred!"

Another Biography of Mr. Li

— Ba Ling

"Mr. Li is truly a peculiar person," is what everyone who knows him says. It turns out that Mr. Li has several strange temperaments that are worth everyone considering strange. They are now written below as another biography of Mr. Li.

First, Mr. Li has no policy regarding the use of money. He uses money when he shouldn't and doesn't use it when he should. This is where his method of using money differs from others. However, this often leads to his financial difficulties. However, when he is in financial difficulty, he has a way to solve his difficulties, which is to "lie down and not get up," and he shouts, "I have no money, so I am resisting here for a long time."

Secondly, Mr. Li's social circle is very wide. It turns out that he considers anyone who has met him once as a lifelong confidant! And he often takes other people's cards and says to people, "This person is how and how, and my relationship with him is how close," but when people ask him to introduce them, Mr. Li always says, "I have only met him once, I'm afraid he doesn't even know me."

Finally, our Mr. Li is very fond of women, especially young women. He is even more welcoming because he is a doctor. When he sees young women coming to him for medical treatment, he even sacrifices fruit to entertain them. On the other hand, if men come to him for medical treatment, if he is not in a good mood, he doesn't even bother to pay attention to them. We all think this temperament is very special.

Therefore, I feel that this Mr. Li is someone who needs to have another biography written for him for publicity purposes.

Oddments Shop

— Zhu Shaofei

When you take expensive fabrics to a tailor to make clothes, they always have to take some material from your fabric, especially leather, which is their best customer. They'll steal a good-quality gray squirrel pelt, cut off several inches of thick fox fur, and they won't even let the ordinary sheepskin go. That's why the lining of our fur coats, after wearing them for a while, will shrink and be an inch or two shorter than the outside. The reason is that when they make them, they're thinking of skimming off your material, stretching the leather, and spraying it with water.

Tailors and assistants have to skim off material to sell to oddments shops, so when we're making expensive fur coats, it's best to tell them beforehand, "If you do a good job, I'll give you some extra money for wine." Otherwise, your clothes will suffer invisible losses.

The largest concentration of oddments shops is in Sanpailou in the city and along Shilu outside the city. In their shops, they sell silks, satins, woolens, and serge, and they also hang up gray squirrel pelts, fox furs, sheepskin cakes, fur collars, and the like. Woolens and serge are mainly sold to people for making shoe uppers or adding trim. Fur goods range from a few inches to entire robe materials and jackets. These are all made from scraps into whole pieces, regardless of the labor involved. So some so-called "old hands" only need to look around oddments shops to choose materials for making fur robes, where the quality is good and the prices are cheap.

Winter is the time when tailors' assistants sell the most goods. Every fifth and tenth day of the month are their so-called "off days" when they stop working at night. Crowds throng in front of the brightly lit oddments shops, noisily trading their goods.

Although tailors' assistants are skilled at skimming off other people's materials, the money vanishes as soon as they get it. They either get into a game of "five hundred spades" or go to gambling dens, or even "hunt wild chickens."

Written to See My Cousin Kunyi Return to Her Teacher Gao Qifeng's Grave

— Ye Gongchuo

A few glimmers of warmth in the depths of a frozen winter,

Her lonely shadow sorrowfully ascends a ten-thousand-mile journey.

Even the sound of ants in their nests can pierce the heavens,

And the sea will dry before the pearls of the shark turn to blood.

Sincerity and devotion will manifest as golden characters,

Her remaining efforts should become a burial mound.

May the weeds in the underworld find some solace,

A single star at dawn is not entirely alone.

Miscellaneous Notes

Fragments of the Sound of Jade

— Wang Fang'an

Cheng is the precious daughter of my friend Cao Mengyu, whose style name is Qingyang. Her given name is Aqi, and she is only ten years old. From birth, she has shown a face of extraordinary intelligence. She remembers everything she reads, and her writing is also quite beautiful. She speaks Western languages fluently. She is currently studying in the fifth grade at Minzhi Elementary School on Weihaiwei Road, where her cleverness surpasses her peers. But unfortunately, on the evening of the fifteenth of the month, she suffered a terrible accident! That evening, Mengyu was carelessly cleaning a gun, and a bullet went astray. Cheng happened to be nearby and was accidentally hit. She died despite medical treatment! A rare talent in the world, like a flash of ephemeral beauty. The tragic news spread, and everyone mourned her loss. My friendship with Mengyu began ten years ago. We did not know each other at first. Later, Mengyu became the editor of the Luotuo Pictorial and moved his family to Shanghai. He brought his wife, Wan, and Cheng, and they lived together on Tongfu Road. I happened to come to Shanghai and made a special visit. At that time, Cheng was only five years old, like a little bird nestled in Wan's arms. She would smile shyly at strangers, but her bright, clear eyes would often stare at me intently. I loved her and stroked her forehead, and she immediately called out "Uncle." I couldn't help but marvel at her quickness. While I was talking with Mengyu, I also heard her sing in a melodious voice, "The Grape Fairy," her tone clear and her words distinct, while she danced and sang. Mengyu and his wife were overjoyed. I often called her a little angel, and in my heart, I deeply admired Mengyu and his wife for their dual blessings of happiness and wisdom; to have such a lovely child to bring them joy. I heard Mengyu say that Cheng had already learned over a thousand characters, all taught by Wan. In the style of Ouyang Xiu and Mengmu, I couldn't help but congratulate Mengyu on having such a virtuous helper. Three years later, I rented a house by the lake. When the osmanthus flowers were fragrant, Mengyu, Wan, and Cheng arrived unannounced to see the Qiantang Tidal Bore. We agreed to be their guide. We traveled for two days, visiting all the scenic spots by the lake. Cheng was already eight years old and dressed like a young girl with her hair hanging down. I asked her how many characters she knew, and it was many more than before. When we were leisurely riding in a small boat in the middle of the lake, Cheng would often say things that made people laugh heartily. It seemed that she had a predestined connection with my wife and me and our deceased son, Tie Ru. She would always interrupt when my wife and I were telling stories about the lake and make Tie Ru laugh with joy, calling him "little brother" in a sweet voice, and even giving him several of her favorite toys. On the day of our departure, Cheng insisted on inviting us to Shanghai during the New Year holiday for a happy gathering, making us reluctant to leave. Her sense of propriety was amazing. That winter, I suffered the loss of Tie Ru and was in a terrible mood. I returned to my hometown to recuperate and stayed at home, and I gradually lost contact with Mengyu. However, every time I woke up from a dream with my wife, after mourning Tie Ru, I couldn't help but think of Cheng. I have been living in seclusion ever since, feeling quite bored. At the beginning of last month, I was invited by Mengyu to come to Shanghai to help him with some matters to relieve my boredom. So I spent time with Cheng day and night, observing her diligence in her studies. I suspected that she was not like other girls of ten years old. Recently, Wan has been busy managing the household and has been slightly less attentive to teaching Cheng, but Cheng's eagerness to ask questions and delve deeper before the lamp is the same as before. Since I came here, she has turned to me to seek deeper knowledge and has insisted that I tutor her in Western languages. I realized that I have neglected this skill for fifteen years and that I can only understand the writing and pronunciation. I couldn't refuse her request, and I was truly ashamed. A month later, I returned to my hometown, and before leaving, I made an agreement to come back and tutor her every Sunday. Although I was reluctant to be a teacher, Cheng was so earnest and repeatedly urged me to come back soon and help her prepare her writing materials. She held onto my clothes, reluctant to let me go, just like a family member. Who would have thought that our final farewell would be in those moments? After returning to my hometown, I often talked to my wife about Cheng's love of learning, deeply regretting that our two daughters were used to being lazy. My wife also often thought about Cheng's cleverness and loveliness, so she asked me to prepare some fruit to take to Cheng as a gift. On the sixteenth, I returned to Shanghai, and after removing the dust of travel, I happened to flip through the newspaper and saw the shocking news of Cheng's death. After recovering from the initial shock, I quickly drove to Mengyu's house. When I arrived, I found that the news was indeed true. Alas! Mengyu, upon seeing me, burst into tears. Wan was sobbing and unable to speak. I was also overcome with grief and could find no words to comfort them. After a long while, I heard Mengyu say, "I have always been careful with my gun, and I never dared to load it with bullets. Recently, because it has been cold and late when I return home, I was afraid of encountering bandits, so I kept it by my side. That night, when I returned home, as usual, I immediately took out the bullets, but I don't know how a bullet ended up remaining in the barrel, causing this tragedy. Afterwards, I decided to comply with the law and reported it to the authorities. At this moment, my heart is aching and filled with remorse. I don't know how to console Aqi in the afterlife." I heard that on the day of Cheng's encoffining, her face looked lifelike, and her smile was sweet. There was no trace of blood from the wound. Could it be that Cheng had completed her time in the human world and returned to her celestial island? I have heard of examples of spiritual liberation and sword dissolution, which might be similar to this. Mengyu is a person of great emotion. This time, he suffered this tragedy and accidentally destroyed his precious daughter. At this moment, I cannot help but offer some absurd words of consolation, hoping to alleviate his sorrow. Mengyu also told me that Cheng has always been loved by friends, and everyone in the literary community has praised her intelligence. In recent days, Mr. Shou Juan, Mu Qin, Kong Wo, Li Qin, and other gentlemen have sent their condolences, and he is deeply grateful for their kindness. They are also planning to collect Cheng's remaining works from school, attach a eulogy, and publish "Records of Withered Ephemerals" to commemorate her.

Imperial Incense: A Fleeting Record

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

At this point, to make us more convinced that what she was saying was not fabricated in any way, the Empress Dowager randomly pointed out several real-life pieces of ironclad evidence. These were many weapons hanging in a large cabinet. The cabinet had no doors, and its position was very sunny, so we could see everything very clearly from the outside. The swords and arrows were mostly rusty, and the bowstrings were rotten, but on each item, there were very noticeable inscriptions, such as: "So-and-so (the name of the leader) used this sword to personally kill a tiger on such-and-such day of such-and-such month in such-and-such year," or "So-and-so used this bow and arrow to hunt a leopard on such-and-such day of such-and-such month in such-and-such year." However, they were all in Manchu, which we naturally couldn't understand. Fortunately, there was a female official who was well-versed in this language to translate for us, so we were able to fully understand. The Empress Dowager also paid close attention to the sentences that the translator produced and had a kind of triumphant expression. Originally, she had only casually guessed that the reason these weapons were so carefully collected was nothing more than to extol the military prowess of her ancestors, so she quickly pointed them out to us. However, she did not expect that her guess was completely correct, so she was naturally very pleased!

In the room on the left, I also discovered something very strange: these were two iron rings that were already very rusty and difficult to look at. The diameter of the rings was probably larger than the wrists of the fattest people. These two rings were hung from the roof beams by two ropes that were not connected, hanging at the same height as the shoulders of a person of average height. The two ropes must have originally been very thick and strong, but now they were moldy and rotten, as if they could be broken immediately with a gentle pull. (221)

Education News

Implementing a Radical and Gradual Approach to Compulsory Education

The proposal by Central Committee member Cai Yuanpei and others has been ordered by the Executive Yuan to be implemented by the Ministry of Education.

The proposal by Central Committee member Cai Yuanpei and eight others to the Fifth Plenary Session of the Central Committee to implement a radical and gradual approach to compulsory education, which was approved by the plenary session and decided by the Central Political Council to be implemented by the National Government, has been instructed by the National Government to the Executive Yuan, which in turn has ordered the Ministry of Education to comply. The original proposal by Committee member Cai and others is as follows:

Proposal for Implementing a Radical and Gradual Approach to Compulsory Education

It is essential to implement compulsory education in our country today. The party's program has a provision for vigorously promoting national education, and the Provisional Constitution during the period of political tutelage also has a provision that all children of school age should receive compulsory education. Most of our people have not received even the most basic education, and compulsory education is essential for implementing national policies, social construction, and overcoming obstacles to the revival of the nation. The old four-year compulsory education system has been vigorously promoted by the central and local education authorities, but due to a lack of funds, a shortage of teachers, and other reasons, the results have been limited. Even today, illiteracy is common in large cities, and even more so in remote rural areas. According to the Ministry of Education's statistics for the 19th year of the Republic (1930), the number of children enrolled in school only accounted for 21.08% of school-age children. At a time when the world situation is pressing, if we do not adopt more effective methods to promote compulsory education in the shortest possible time, the future of the nation is truly worrying. The Ministry of Education has previously formulated primary school regulations, which went through the legislative process and were promulgated by the National Government in December of the 21st year of the Republic (1932). In addition, there are the General Outline for the First Phase of Compulsory Education and the General Outline for the Implementation of Short-Term Compulsory Education, which were promulgated by the ministry in June of the 21st year of the Republic, and four volumes of short-term primary school textbooks have been compiled and distributed for use. In addition, there is a general order for primary schools to adopt the two-shift system. However, because there is no mandatory law to require provinces and cities to comply, the strictness and speed of implementation vary greatly. The above-mentioned methods are summarized below, and suggestions are put forward as follows:

(1) Short-term compulsory education with a one-year time limit should be implemented to enforce education for out-of-school children aged ten to sixteen. This is a radical approach.

In the 9th year of the Republic (1920), there were laws and regulations for compulsory education, with a promotion period of one year. After the establishment of the National Government, the Second National Education Conference changed the promotion period of compulsory education to 20 years. However, the targets of promotion are all four years. The cost of compulsory education is huge, and the number of teachers required is large. Judging from the national financial resources, social economy, and the actual situation of existing teachers, the gap is far too great. To achieve the goal of universal education, the day of achieving it seems to be indefinitely postponed. The previously promulgated Measures for Short-term Compulsory Education were concluded as an emergency policy to adapt to the special environment of our country. The duration of compulsory education is temporarily shortened to a short-term one year. Primary schools or short-term primary school classes allow out-of-school children aged ten to sixteen to receive two hours of education in shifts every day, and tuition fees are waived and books and supplies are provided so that poor children can work while attending school for free. Over the past 20 years, the central and local authorities have promoted and implemented compulsory education, which cannot be said to be ineffective. However, the reason why it takes a long time, a lot of effort, and little effect is that the funds and teachers required for four years of compulsory education are also too large. Short-term primary schools or short-term primary school classes employ a teacher in the morning, afternoon, and evening to teach three classes of out-of-school children. Counting 40 children per class, 120 children can graduate in one year. Compared with ordinary primary school children in two classes, 40 children per class, graduating in four years, only 80 children, the disparity in the amount of funding is 1 to 18. The curriculum of short-term primary schools or short-term primary school classes is only literacy, simple common sense, and simple arithmetic, which is very easy to teach, but slightly more advanced than the current civilian schools. Anyone who knows how to read and write can take the job. Therefore, its teachers are not limited to those who have received teacher training and have any teaching experience. The situation is different from ordinary middle school courses with many teachers, who must be strictly tested. The previous General Outline for the Implementation of Measures stipulated that in addition to hiring qualified teachers, the following personnel should be fully utilized: (1) teacher-training students from local normal schools or rural normal schools who are about to complete their internship; (2) teachers who have received considerable training and can be used as substitute teachers; (3) local civil servants; (4) local people with considerable education; (5) volunteers who are willing to serve as teachers and fulfill their obligations. The teacher qualifications are specially relaxed. This is a common fact when countries begin to implement compulsory education. Furthermore, older students have stronger learning abilities, and the effect of one year may be almost the same as that of a six-year-old entering school and receiving four years of education. And older people can go out and serve as soon as they graduate. In terms of the entire society, it is equivalent to increasing a large number of literate young people every year. All countries implement compulsory education, starting with the promotion of primary school education, making primary school education compulsory, and gradually extending the length of compulsory education. There are too many illiterates in our country, and the financial resources are too tight. Compulsory education and primary school education cannot be combined into one thing. For older out-of-school children, shortening the length of compulsory education in order to achieve rapid popularization is a last resort. Based on the above reasons, it is proposed that the central government stipulate that the 24th year of the Republic (1935) shall be the starting period for the implementation of compulsory education, temporarily with a period of four years, and designate short-term primary schools or short-term primary school classes as places for the implementation of compulsory education, and implement compulsory education for older out-of-school children aged ten to sixteen.

(2) Pay attention to vigorously promoting primary school education and earnestly implement the half-day two-shift system. This is a fundamental approach.

The aforementioned short-term compulsory education is specially designed for saving older out-of-school children. In order to increase the enrollment opportunities for school-age children and improve the efficiency of ordinary primary school education, it is essential to promote and enrich primary school education. The previously established Primary School Law and Primary School Regulations have strict regulations on local education research, primary school staffing, financial allocation, equipment enrichment, moral education reform, and teacher treatment. Special attention is paid to the curriculum in order to enable existing primary schools to comply with these regulations and enrich their content. In the General Outline for the First Phase of Compulsory Education, the procedures for phased and regional implementation are specified in order to gradually achieve universal coverage. However, phased and regional implementation requires years of teacher training. Although simplified normal schools, simplified normal departments, and vocational normal departments have been added in addition to ordinary normal schools, this is still too slow to respond to emergencies, and it is impossible to train a large number of talents in a short period of time. Therefore, another emergency method must be considered. What is this method? It is the adoption of the two-shift system. According to the statistics of the 19th year of the Republic (1930), there were 250,840 primary schools and kindergartens in the country, 568,484 primary school teachers, and 10,994,8979 children in school. On average, each school only has 44 children, and each teacher only teaches 19 children. Such uneconomical practices are rare in the world. Countries with developed education and economies far superior to ours have more children taught by each teacher than we do. It is unreasonable for our country's poverty to reverse this waste. The danger to the future of the country is also unimaginable. The two-shift system is an excellent way to expand and develop primary school education without increasing the existing amount of funding and teachers. After the European War, some countries have adopted it one after another and achieved significant results. The half-day two-shift system is particularly suitable for the current economic principles of our country, as there is no need to add school buildings and games and rest places. In terms of the benefits for children, the two-shift system is slightly inferior to ordinary primary schools, but the difference is not too great. Furthermore, for the sake of the entire society, it is reasonable to slightly reduce the educational happiness of a few school-age children for the sake of the majority of out-of-school children in order to fulfill the duty of mutual assistance. After the two-shift system is implemented, the expenses and teachers of each primary school only need to be slightly increased, and the number of children can be doubled. In other words, one school can be used as two schools, and the number of primary schools in the country will double immediately. At the same time, the existing primary schools will be utilized to the maximum extent and the enrollment will be increased, so that the number of children entering school can be increased several times, and gradually it will be universalized to all school-age children. Based on the above reasons, it is proposed that the central government actively promote the nationwide primary schools to earnestly implement the half-day two-shift system by order of the National Government. The places where primary schools in villages and cities cannot meet the demand should strive to follow the above. At the same time, the teachers of private schools should be trained to make up for the deficiencies of the above-mentioned teacher training.

As for the source of funding for the above-mentioned compulsory education, there are detailed regulations in the Implementation Measures. The main points are that in addition to raising funds locally, the competent education administrative agencies should be requested to provide subsidies. However, the number of local funds that are insufficient after compulsory education is implemented will be even greater. It is proposed that the central government, starting from the 24th year of the Republic (1935), designate special funds to provide subsidies, and order each province and city, starting from the 24th year of the Republic (1935), to allocate special funds for the implementation of short-term compulsory education and the promotion of the primary school two-shift system. (Check the resolutions on education of the third plenary session of the fourth Central Executive Committee on December 21 of the 20th year of the Republic (1931), (A) Regarding national education, items 2 and 3 have regulations on this matter and are combined with a statement.) Whether the above-mentioned measures for compulsory education are appropriate is respectfully awaiting public decision. Proposers: Cai Yuanpei, Ye Chucang, Dai Chuanxian, Ding Weifen, Zhu Peide, Song Ziwen, He Yingqin, Wu Jingheng, Zhu Jiahua.

The Science Society of China Held a Joint Meeting of Directors and Supervisors Yesterday

Cai Yuanpei Presided and Reported on Society Affairs

Xu Xinliu Succeeded as Custodian of the Fund

The Science Society of China held a joint meeting of directors and supervisors yesterday at 3:00 PM at the society's office on Avenue Albert. Attendees included Cai Yuanpei, Sun Ke, Song Hanzhang, Xu Xinliu, Hu Dunfu, Wu Liande, Yang Xiaoshu, Zhou Ren, Hu Gangfu, and over ten others. Chairman Cai Yuanpei first reported on the purpose of the meeting and the society's affairs. Then, various proposals were discussed. The most important was that Song Hanzhang, the custodian of the society's fund, had repeatedly requested to resign due to old age and hearing loss. He officially handed over the position yesterday, and Xu Xinliu was publicly elected to succeed him. An inventory was taken on the spot. It was reported that Mr. Song had been in charge of the society's fund for six and a half years. During this period, the society purchased land for offices in Beijing and Shanghai, and constructed a library and research institute, and added books, costing a total of over 280,000 yuan. The society's fund was not large to begin with, and all the construction costs were originally obtained by mortgaging the fund. Everyone thought that the fund must have been greatly affected, but because Mr. Song handled it effectively, it was able to be fully preserved by the end of last year's settlement. This shows Mr. Song's expertise as a veteran in the economic field, and his hard work in managing public funds. Therefore, the society's colleagues expressed their warm thanks. Mr. Song indicated that he would continue to assist in the society's affairs from the sidelines in the future. The meeting concluded at around 5:00 PM.

National Library Statistics for Universities and Colleges

The Ministry of Education has compiled statistics for various types of books in national universities, colleges, and specialized schools for the 21st year of the Republic. A summary is recorded below:

(1) Total books in various categories in national universities, colleges, and specialized schools in the 21st year of the Republic: 756,395 volumes (National universities, colleges, and specialized schools totaled 216,219 volumes, Ministry-run specialized schools 6,803 volumes, Provincial universities, colleges, and specialized schools totaled 132,793 volumes, Private universities, colleges, and specialized schools totaled 400,580 volumes.)

(2) Philosophy books: 155,279 volumes in total, with 72,345 volumes in the national sector, 263 volumes in the Ministry-run sector, 19,104 volumes in the provincial sector, and 63,667 volumes in the private sector.

(3) Religion books: 54,512 volumes in total, with 9,593 volumes in the national sector, 421 volumes in the Ministry-run sector, 4,197 volumes in the provincial sector, and 40,301 volumes in the private sector.

(4) Social Science books: 324,014 volumes in total, with 108,341 volumes in the national sector, 1,514 volumes in the Ministry-run sector, 69,145 volumes in the provincial sector, and 145,005 volumes in the private sector.

(5) Language books: 71,533 volumes in total, with 25,204 volumes in the national sector, 456 volumes in the Ministry-run sector, 10,191 volumes in the provincial sector, and 35,682 volumes in the private sector.

(6) Natural Science books: 152,821 volumes in total, with 54,588 volumes in the national sector, 142 volumes in the Ministry-run sector, 25,291 volumes in the provincial sector, and 72,800 volumes in the private sector.

(7) Applied Science books: 178,236 volumes in total, with 56,411 volumes in the national sector, 11,125 volumes in the Ministry-run sector, 32,170 volumes in the provincial sector, and 78,530 volumes in the private sector.

(8) Fine Arts books: 63,707 volumes in total, with 23,478 volumes in the national sector, 724 volumes in the Ministry-run sector, 5,431 volumes in the provincial sector, and 34,074 volumes in the private sector.

(9) Literature books: 423,242 volumes in total, with 140,255 volumes in the national sector, 2,408 volumes in the Ministry-run sector, 103,357 volumes in the provincial sector, and 177,222 volumes in the private sector.

(10) History and Geography books: 366,270 volumes in total, with 142,837 volumes in the national sector, 2,982 volumes in the Ministry-run sector, 81,104 volumes in the provincial sector, and 393,471 volumes in the private sector.

The total number of books above is 3,951,847 volumes. Among them, national universities, colleges, and specialized schools have a total of 1,420,954 volumes. Ministry-run specialized schools have a total of 28,138 volumes. Provincial universities, colleges, and specialized schools have a total of 512,228 volumes. Private universities, colleges, and specialized schools have a total of 1,990,527 volumes.

Sports News: The International Football League's Reigning Champion Loses Its Position

Portugal Eliminates England

The Portuguese Army is Fearsome, Winning the Finals with Six Against Two

The Sino-Portuguese Final Will Inevitably be a Great Show

In the semi-finals of the Western Union Football International Cup, the China-Russia match was suspended due to the field being unusable, but the Portugal-England group played as usual at the Racecourse. Portugal eliminated England by a huge score of six to two. England was the reigning champion, and this signifies their loss of position. The resurgence of Portugal is also remarkably vigorous and surprising. In the first half, Portugal dominated and took the lead with four to one. The situation in the second half was no longer the same. England only scored one goal, while Portugal added two more goals, resulting in a final score of six to two. Given the ferocity of Portugal at the moment, it is difficult to predict the outcome of the Sino-Portuguese final.

The Liangjiang Basketball Team Defeats Yiling

Traveling to Qingpu for a Match This Morning

Last night, Liangjiang played against Yiling at the Navy YMCA, starting at 8:30 PM. Since Liangjiang adopted the men's rules, they have won big victories in the first match against the American Union and the second match against the Anglo-American mixed team. The victory against the West Women's Yiling last night was also expected. In the first quarter, Liangjiang was defeated. Liangjiang seemed to be not very energetic. Within five minutes, Chen Rongming scored the first point. At this time, the competition between the two sides was quite fierce. Yiling relied on its height and strength to gain a lot of advantages. The scorekeeper called and wrote Yiling 6 and Liangjiang 3 on the blackboard. The second quarter was evenly matched. After a short break, the war started again. Liangjiang used a five-person defense, and the Yiling team was not as rampant as before. Chen Rongming and Chen Jucai of the Liangjiang team were heroic and vigorous, and the two guards also did their best, snatching and seizing the ball, and putting the enemy to death. In the third and fourth quarters, the Yiling team gradually showed signs of being unable to support themselves, and made no achievements in the fourth quarter. The Liangjiang team, which had lost first, seemed like a sea dragon at this time, agile and lively, and defended and attacked properly, which made Yiling at a loss. As a result, Liangjiang won 25 to 14. The Liangjiang A team is scheduled to go to Qingpu for a match at 9:00 AM this morning. The group of fourteen people is led by Zhang Yuansheng, the dean of academic affairs of the school, and Coach Hu Zhengqu. It is also heard that the Qingpu Chamber of Commerce Sports Association specially invited Qian Jiaxiang, the county magistrate of the county, and Huang Peize, the standing committee member of the county party department, to perform the opening kickoff ceremony, it was said. The match schedule is recorded as follows: (1) Against the Qingpu Chamber of Commerce Red Team at 3:00 PM on the 14th, (2) Against the Qingpu Chamber of Commerce Green Team at 3:00 PM on the 15th, (3) Visit Sheshan Mountain on the morning of the 16th and return to Shanghai in the afternoon.

Financial Weekly Call Loan Rate Drops Another Two Cents

The silver market has been gradually declining recently, and yesterday was Sunday, with banks closed, making the situation even more sluggish. As a result, the call loan rate continued to weaken, with both the morning and afternoon markets at 21 cents, a further drop of two cents from the previous day. Call loan transactions: over 1.5 million in the morning market, over 600,000 in new transactions, over 400,000 in the afternoon market, over 700,000 in the Small General Association, over 300,000 in silver pawn redemptions, over 500,000 in new loans, over 200,000 in banknote redemptions, over 27 million in bank drafts from money shops, and over 300,000 in remittances from various routes. Due to the bank holiday, all collection activities were suspended. The auxiliary coin market is also softening daily. Jiangnan small silver once fell below one yuan in the morning market, to 846 yuan. Although it returned to 847 yuan in the afternoon market, there was still no change compared to the previous day. Guangdong small silver also fell by one yuan in the morning market, opening at 758.5 yuan, and changing to 758.4 yuan in the afternoon market, resulting in a slight decrease of one yuan and one dime compared to the previous day. Transactions: 3,000 jiao of Jiangnan coins and 120,000 jiao of Guangdong coins in the morning market, 4,000 jiao of Jiangnan coins and 90,000 jiao of Guangdong coins in the afternoon market. Copper coins also decreased by 1,000 wen compared to the previous day, to 306,000 wen, with a transaction volume of 29,988 strings of wen, equivalent to 9,800 yuan.

Theoretical Points on Taxation of Securities and Securities Broker Transactions

Debt Transfer…Why Charge Fees?

Yesterday afternoon, the entire body of brokers at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange held a general meeting on the eighth floor of the Securities Building to discuss the government's recent preparation to levy transaction taxes. The number of attendees was extremely enthusiastic. First, the chairman and vice-chairman of the Brokers Association announced the progress and their work. There were many speeches at the meeting. Everyone believed that the government has issued public bonds and treasury bills for many years, with the amount already around 100 million yuan. They rely on the brokers to widely promote and sell them, which has resulted in an astonishing achievement. Brokers have made an essential contribution. The obligation to pay taxes is not something brokers object to. However, public bonds and treasury bills are government-issued debt instruments. No country in the world levies transaction taxes on them. Even when the government issues documents and contracts for official business, there is never a stamp tax. This shows that public bonds cannot be compared to goods such as yarn, flour, and miscellaneous grains. It is also like borrowing money in the private sector. If the debtor wants to charge the creditor a fee when the debt is transferred, it is unreasonable. As a result, everyone unanimously opposed the tax and jointly elected the chairman of the association to actively request the government to exempt or postpone the tax with the chairman of the exchange.

Yarn and Raw Cotton Both Decline

Yesterday, US cotton opened lower because of poor news from Liverpool. Foreign merchants sold, and each month fell by one to four pounds. Occasionally, there was no movement. Later, Wall Street was sluggish, and sentiment softened further. At the close, there was some short covering, which slightly strengthened the market. Spot prices fell by 9 points, and futures prices fell by 7-8 points. Indian cotton fell due to selling by Japanese merchants and hedging by cotton farmers. Pingguo'er fell by 3.25 Robbie, Aomura fell by 6 Robbie, and Bairoxi fell by 5.75 Robbie. Original telegraph on the left (12th telegram).

Shen Bao Medical Weekly

Table of

General Situation of Medical and Health in Nanning City

— Zhichang

Nanning is the political center of Guangxi. In recent years, the opening of roads and the expansion of urban areas have been completed in order. Therefore, it is more prosperous and lively than in the past, the population has doubled, and the sanitary facilities are slightly more complete than in the past. However, the medical and pharmaceutical equipment has not developed much. Now, I will briefly describe the current situation of medical and health in the city as follows:

(1) Public Health Facilities

Public health is fully handled by the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau. Its facilities can be divided into the following items: (1) Cleaning - Regarding cleaning, garbage dumping grounds are set up in remote areas. If the streets and alleys are far away from the garbage dump, public garbage bins are hung. The Public Security Bureau manufactures garbage trucks, and orders the servants to push them to the streets and alleys with garbage bins every day at a scheduled time and frequency to dump the garbage in the bins. They also stop at a place for a certain period of time, ringing the bell as a sign, so that all the garbage of the residents in the street can be dumped into the garbage truck. In addition, sanitation workers are hired to sweep the streets twice a day, and the Public Security Bureau issues an order to the whole city to carry out a major cleaning twice a year, disinfecting the city's ditches, public toilets, public urinals, public spittoons, etc. with medicinal water. (2) Health Care - Regarding health care, the sale of all unsanitary food and beverages is prohibited, illegal doctors and midwives are banned, sick animals are prohibited from being slaughtered, inspection teams are organized to inspect the sanitary facilities of public toilets, kitchens and toilets of each household, theaters, and restaurants in the city. (3) Epidemic Prevention - Regarding epidemic prevention, cowpox is vaccinated free of charge every year. Hospitals and doctors in the city are hired as voluntary positions. Every summer, hospitals and doctors in the city are convened to form an epidemic prevention committee to administer various epidemic prevention vaccines to citizens free of charge, carry out fly eradication campaigns, and set up rat boxes in various streets. The above is about the implementation of public health. As for publicity, leaflets or pictorials with texts such as various disease prevention methods and key points of personal hygiene are printed and distributed. This is a general overview of public health.

(2) Current Situation of Hospitals

There are a total of five hospitals and one Red Cross Society in Nanning City. The Red Cross Society has no facilities for hospitalization and only does emergency work. Among the five hospitals, one is a public military hospital, three are established by churches, and one is private. The best equipped and largest in scale is the military hospital, which has fourteen new doctors. It has solar lamps, X-rays, electrotherapy and other equipment. However, only soldiers and students receiving military training are allowed to be hospitalized. Those who are hospitalized do not have to pay any fees, only a meal fee of 30 cents per day. Officers and soldiers are treated equally. Surgical fees, injection fees, and oral medicine fees are all waived. Although ordinary people are not allowed to be hospitalized, they are allowed to enter the hospital for diagnosis and treatment at a certain time every day. All kinds of fees are charged, but they are slightly cheaper than other hospitals. Among the three hospitals established by the church, one has one new doctor, one has three new doctors, and one has two new doctors. The equipment is not very complete, and they are all ordinary equipment. There are no X-rays. The minimum hospitalization fee is two yuan per day, and the minimum injection fee is five yuan per injection. The surgical fee is determined according to the severity of the illness. If you do not stay in the hospital and go to the hospital for consultation, the consultation fee is one yuan each time, and the medicine fee and injection fee are given according to the price set by the hospital. The above four hospitals have a certain time every day to provide free diagnosis and treatment to benefit the poor and sick. One of the private hospitals has one Chinese medicine doctor and no equipment, and the cost is not detailed.

The current situation of the five hospitals is listed below:

Name Doctor Establishment Annual Public Funding

Guangxi Military Hospital 14 (Western) Public 110,000 yuan

Rose Hospital 3 (Western) Church
