Paradise Hospital 2 (Western) Church

Puji Hospital 1 (Chinese) Private

(3) Current Situation of Private Clinics and Pharmacies

There are a total of 129 old doctors and 38 new doctors in Nanning City. Comparing the medical skills of the two, the old doctors are better. This is of course in general terms. If they are famous doctors, their medical skills will be very prosperous. The reasons for this phenomenon can be divided into several points: (1) The cost of old doctors is cheaper, and the price of medicine is not expensive. If they are new doctors, they have spent a lot of money and financial resources when they were studying medicine. When they graduate and practice medicine, the equipment of medical instruments also costs a lot, so the remuneration they take is naturally higher. In addition, the medicine comes from overseas, and the tax is very heavy when it is transported to the interior, so the price of medicine is also expensive. The old doctors do not need any equipment, and their medical skills are mostly inherited from their ancestors, so they do not need to spend much money, so the price they take is also cheaper. Usually, the consultation fee for old doctors is only a few cents per visit, while the consultation fee for new doctors is one yuan. If the disease needs to be injected, the cost is even greater. Therefore, ordinary people seek help from old doctors in order to reduce the burden. (2) New doctors without medical ethics cheat and make people lose faith in new doctors - Some new doctors without medical ethics take advantage of the fact that ordinary people do not know the cost of new medicines and do not know what medicine to use for what disease. Therefore, when treating a patient, they want to prevent the patient from recovering quickly in order to get more money. They often give unimportant medicines to take internally, or inject distilled water and say that they are injecting a certain medicine, which costs a certain amount. This makes the patient spend a lot of money, and the pain cannot be relieved. Therefore, they turn to old doctors and get better. The patient immediately publicizes that new doctors are useless. There are few such doctors, but they are indeed moths in the new medical community. (3) Because the equipment of private clinics is simpler than that of hospitals, people who are sick and want to seek help from new doctors see that the equipment of private clinics is incomplete and go to hospitals more often. This is also the reason why private clinics are unpopular.

Now let's briefly talk about pharmacies. There are 59 Chinese pharmacies and 16 Western pharmacies in Nanning. The business of pharmacies depends on the prosperity of doctors' clinics, but there are many over-the-counter drugs in Western pharmacies. People with sufficient economic means see that their methods of taking are convenient, and they do not need to consult a doctor, so many people buy them.

(Editor's note) - Mr. Zhichang put forward three reasons why new medicine in Nanning is not developed: (1) Medical expenses are too expensive, (2) Affected by unethical new doctors: (3) Incomplete equipment. Among these three points, except for the second point that new doctors need to work hard on their own, the other two points are related to the economy. We hope that the new medical community will unite and that the government will do its best to help and support this budding of new medicine.

Common Sense Q&A About Diseases

— Cheng Hanzhang

(51) Relapsing Fever

(Q) What is Relapsing Fever?

(A) This is an epidemic or local infectious disease. It is caused by several spirochetes parasitizing in the blood.

(Q) What is the Western name for this disease?

(A) The German name is Euckfallfieber; the Latin name is Febris recurrens; the English name is recurrent fever or relapsing fever. They all mean fever that comes again.

(Q) Who discovered the pathogenic spirochete of relapsing fever?

(A) As far as we know now, there are seven or eight kinds of spirochetes that cause relapsing fever. The first one discovered is called Spironma Bbermeier, which was discovered by Mr. Obermeier. This refers to a type that is prevalent in Europe. In addition, there are several types found in Africa. There are also several spirochetes found in America, India and Persia. They are all different.

(Q) How are relapsing fever spirochetes spread?

(A) It is spread by many blood-sucking insects. Like bed bugs and lice can spread it.

(Q) Which part of the body is the main lesion of relapsing fever?

(A) The spleen is the main one. Therefore, the patient's spleen must be enlarged, softened, bleeding, or necrotic. Suppurative and other changes.

(Q) Will the disease develop immediately after infection?

(A) There is an incubation period of five to eight days from infection to the onset of the disease.

(Q) What happens when the disease breaks out?

(A) At the beginning of the disease, you will definitely feel chills and high fever (often 41 degrees). At the same time, the skin is dirty yellow, dry, and has a fever.

(Q) What does the patient feel like after that?

(A) After that, there will be severe headaches, accompanied by sacral pain and limb pain. There is hypersensitivity or tenderness to touch in the muscles everywhere. Especially the fibula muscle of the lower leg is even more severe.

(Q) Are there any other symptoms?

(A) Other symptoms include frequent pulse, vomiting, diarrhea, and creeping rash on the lips.

(Q) How do you know if the spleen is diseased?

(A) The spleen swells significantly and rapidly. It can often be felt under the costal arch and is tender to the touch. The liver is also slightly swollen.

(Q) What is the mental state of the patient?

(Q) The patient's consciousness is usually clear, but sometimes there is a desireless state, lethargy, or delirium. Sometimes there is tremulous delirium.

(Q) How many days does this fever period last? How does the fever go down?

(A) This will last for six or seven days. Afterwards, the fever subsides with profuse sweating.

(Q) Can the symptoms completely disappear after the fever subsides?

(A) After the fever subsides, various symptoms can disappear. The spleen also shrinks. The pulse becomes slow. The patient feels very refreshed.

One Year of Chinese Medicine and Hygiene (2)

— Jiang Huiming

Introduction - Medical Education - Medical Group Activities - Medical Disputes - Medical Publishing - Medical Inspections - Medical Construction - Military Medical Training - A Glimpse of the Old Medical Field - Trends in the New Pharmaceutical Industry - Rural Hygiene Survey - Urban Hygiene Perspectives - Conclusion

(III) Medical Group Activities

Medical group activities have indeed entered a period of significant transformation in the 23rd year. Please elaborate:

In the spring of the 23rd year, the Third National Physicians' Association was held in the capital, bringing together elites from the north and south, and renowned scholars from the east and west. It also received support and assistance from virtuous individuals in the government, garnering praise from public opinion and attention from society. It showed signs of vigorous development in scientific medicine, like a bud about to burst into bloom. When we occasionally trace historical precedents, we realize that Japanese scientific medicine advanced rapidly after the Meiji Restoration due to the driving force of political and legal power. The slow progress of Chinese scientific medicine is because of the lack of political support. Therefore, politics serves as a major driving force in the development of medicine. Now, in the Third National Physicians' Association, renowned figures of the Party and the nation were aware of the importance of this meeting and deeply understood the relationship between medicine and the nation. They made efforts to promote it amidst the high tide of national rejuvenation, predicting that Chinese scientific medicine will have considerable progress due to this meeting.

Even more gratifying is that the Chinese Medical Association and the Ninth Far Eastern Tropical Medicine Association were held in Beijing one after another in the past year. The specialized research achievements presented were voluminous, mostly crystallizations of the hard work of Chinese scholars, washing away the shame of China's lack of medical research talent in the international arena! With the convening of this meeting, the future of Chinese medicine is bright, with a

Page 16

active and ever-changing atmosphere. However, upon further investigation, there is still something that deserves our serious reflection: many Chinese scholars who made special contributions in this conference were mostly conducting research while working under foreign institutions. For example, Mr. Lin Zongyang, Yu He, Tao Chison, Yang Shuzu, Gu Jingqian and others were either at the Radium Institute in Shanghai, the Peking Union Medical College, or the Natural Science Institute in Shanghai, essentially working for others. This is something we deeply regret. China is an independent country. How can we not have our own medical research institutions to serve as places for nurturing talent and conducting research? We hope that our colleagues in the field and government authorities will actively plan and establish them to strive for supreme glory in the international medical community in the future.

Secondly, the Chinese Pharmaceutical Association of the Republic of China, through the efforts of Mr. Yu Yunxiu, Chen Fangzhi, Wang Qizhang, Guo Qiyuan, and Chen Zhuoren, has also made astonishing progress in the past year. The documents published in each issue of the New Medicine and Pharmaceuticals journal hosted by the association fully demonstrate the symbol of extreme progress.

There is one more thing that we must mention with heartfelt emotion: the signs of disintegration within the Chinese scientific medical community in the 23rd year have yet to be completely eliminated. During this period, Messrs. Song Guobin, Pang Jingzhou, Wang Qizhang, and Chen Fangzhi engaged in written discussions. Until now, the call to eliminate medical factions and achieve medical group cooperation has not yet been realized! We do not know when there will be hope for reviving the banner of "cooperation."

(IV) Medical Disputes

The 23rd year can be described as the year of medical disputes. The number of medical disputes in this year far exceeded our expectations. The most prominent cases, such as those involving Yu Songyun, Qiu Boxun, Shen Kefei, Zhang Xiangwen, Ge Chenghui, Lin Huizhen, Li Yuanshan, and Gu Zongwen, can be said to have caused a national sensation. Fortunately, legal principles were not abandoned, and academic principles were not extinguished, so they were all able to overturn wrongful convictions and avoid being framed. However, there are still people who have fallen into the legal net due to medical disputes, such as Liu Maochun, the director of the dermatology department of the Jiangxi Provincial Hospital, and his assistant, who were sentenced to imprisonment. This trend is rampant, and every doctor is in danger.

From a medical standpoint, it is difficult for us to assess the rights and wrongs, fearing that we might be biased. Some believe that there are absolutely no doctors who are useless and misdiagnose patients. However, examining the causes of past disputes, the doctors who were accused were not at genuine fault. Most disputes were due to financial issues, instigation by petty people, emotional misunderstandings, blame shifting among colleagues, and even attempts to obtain compensation without regard for the doctor's reputation. Such a perverse atmosphere cannot be ignored.

The purpose of medicine is to maintain human health and achieve natural death. However, although today's level of medicine has everything, the deterioration of disease mechanisms can still lurk and erupt at any time. As such, how can those who practice medicine absolutely guarantee that patients will not die? If simply failing to restore a patient's health after diagnosis and treatment constitutes grounds for suspicion of professional negligence, then the number of such cases will be as numerous as the sands of the Ganges! The future is long, so how should we eliminate such unexpected disputes? It is necessary to make a decision urgently.

First - The power of medical administration should be brought into play: strictly crack down on itinerant doctors - doctors without formal medical school backgrounds, doctors who have not been reviewed and registered by the Department of Health - to raise the status of doctors and firmly demonstrate the faith of the public. Second - Medical lawsuits should be adjudicated impartially: the medical and legal professions should quickly organize a "Public Adjudication Office" for medical lawsuits. All formal doctors who are accused should first be subject to public adjudication by the Public Adjudication Office, and then be subject to legal sanctions after the adjudication determines the truth. Third - Implement a medical jury system! If there are medical lawsuit cases, the court should send a letter to the academic society to select renowned medical experts to attend court as jurors so that judges can have convenient access to consultations. Fourth - Forensic medical appraisals should be requested: the Zhenru Forensic Medicine Research Institute has achieved many successes in non-medical litigation cases it has handled over the past year. In the future, medical litigation cases should be submitted for forensic medical appraisal within a relevant scope. Fifth - Severe punishment should be given to those who fabricate accusations so that litigious individuals do not dare to easily test the law. The above are the general outlines of my humble opinion. I deeply hope that honest colleagues in the field, enlightened citizens, impartial officials, and patients of integrity will pay attention to and study them.

(V) Medical Publishing

The development of medical publishing and the excellence of printing technology are two parallel lines that develop in the same direction. In European and American countries, as well as neighboring Japan, the development of medical publishing is due to the diligent research of a group of scholars, but the excellence of printing technology is the biggest reason for promoting the development of medical publishing. This is because realistic color illustrations and radiopaque images in medicine are difficult to make satisfactory without good printing. In China's medical publishing industry: there are few research talents and no excellent printing, so progress in the past year has been extremely slow. In terms of medical books, the ones published in the 23rd year include the Internal Medicine translated by Wu Xiangfeng and others, published by the Japanese Dojinkai, and the Physiology co-translated by Zhou Songsheng and others. The Synopsis of Surgery translated by Liu Zhaolin, published by the Beiping Medical Journal, and the Internal Medicine Diagnosis and Treatment Medical Dictionary compiled by Chen Gongsu. The Medical Circle Guide co-edited by Song Guobin and Zhu Hengbi, published by the Chinese Medical Association, and the Emergency Treatment of the British Red Cross Society translated by Lu Dexing. As for those published privately: there are only a dozen or so titles such as the Cholera Outline co-authored by Wu Liande and others, the Pathology authored by Huang Manou, the Pharmacology compiled by Zhang Xiaozong, the Gonorrhea Truth compiled by Xie Junshou, the Bone Fracture Treatment translated by Niu Huisheng and others, the Pediatric Infectious Diseases authored by Gao Jinglang, the Medical Common Sense authored by Tao Chison, the Crude Drug Science co-authored by Zhao Yu, Huang Xubo, and Yun, and the Latest Internal Medicine Treatment Complete Book compiled by Yao Bolin. As for the medical and health series newly published by the Department of Health, Commercial Press, China Book Company, Datong Book Company, and Beixin Book Company, the number is extremely scarce, and compared with the endless stream of medical masterpieces from various countries abroad, we are truly far behind! Moreover, the simplicity of printing is even more needless to say.

In the 23rd year, there was no significant progress in medical journals and publications. The only ones that were barely satisfactory were the past Chinese Pharmaceutical Association of the Republic of China Journal, which is now merged with the Southeast Medical Journal, Social Medical Report, and Scientific Medical Report to form the New Medicine and Pharmaceuticals; and the Chinese Medical Journal published by the Chinese Medical Association, which is now changed to a monthly magazine, edited by Mr. Yu Yunxiu. The contents of the two journals often focus on research and investigation documents, and the richness of the materials can be said to be unparalleled in domestic medical journals. Journals such as the Social Medicine and Pharmaceutical News, now changed to the Social Medicine and Pharmaceutical Monthly, can be said to be on par with the Medical and Pharmaceutical Review in the field of medical commentary, which is another transformation. As for newly published ones, such as the Forensic Medicine Monthly, Medical Affairs Public Opinion, the Medical Weekly of the News Evening Post, the Dental Weekly, the Venereal Disease Bi-Monthly, the Anti-Tuberculosis Monthly, the Southeast School Voice, and the Hebei Public Hygiene Magazine, there are not more than a dozen or so, which clearly shows the desolation of China's medical publishing industry.

(VI) Medical Inspections

The stones of other mountains can be used to polish jade. Since Chinese medicine is in its budding and growing stage, the matter of inspection cannot be delayed. Lessons can be learned from the inspection to improve Chinese medicine. The Chinese people have often neglected the importance of medical inspections. Over the past year, graduates from medical schools have made several graduation visits, but most have no statistical reports. It is just a cursory glance, with little meaning to speak of. Formal domestic medical and health institutions that can send staff abroad for inspection are almost non-existent! Dr. Wu Zhijian, sent by the Shanghai Leprosy Association to Europe for inspection in the 23rd year, was a special discovery, as rare as Dr. Wu Liande's going abroad for inspection. Mr. Weng Zhilong's inspection in the Northwest, amid the development of the Northwest, is also a valuable page.

What is gratifying is that the Ministry of Education seems to have the determination to reorganize medical education over the past year. In the 23rd year, it first appointed Mr. Pang Jingzhou and others to inspect medical schools in North China, and Mr. Yan Fuqing and others to inspect medical schools in East China. Although this is a supervisory nature, it is also related to the improvement of medical education. We deeply hope that based on the findings of the investigation, a direction for future medical education can be established in the shortest possible time to correct the mistakes of China's past medical education, which had no direction.

(VII) Medical Construction

In the context of a national economy that is gradually moving towards chronic bankruptcy, it is difficult to talk about medical construction. However, the addition of hospitals in various places often has no opportunity for public announcement, making it difficult to investigate. Now, taking Shanghai as an example, there are still some new creations in the 23rd year, such as the Hongqiao Sanatorium, which has simple and magnificent architecture and is extremely reasonable. As for the medical schools and hospitals under construction but not yet completed, there are the Shanghai Medical College and the Red Cross Hospital, which will build magnificent buildings at the Shanghai Baseball Field, the new practice hall of the Southeast Medical College will soon be completed, the new five-story building of Guangzi Hospital will soon be completed, and the Tongde Medical College is designing and building a school building. These are all new developments in the past year. In addition, the Jiangxi Medical College added school buildings, and the Guangxi Provincial Government is planning to establish a medical school. We all deeply hope that they can be completed soon.

(VIII) Military Medical Training

At the eve of the world war, amid the active expansion of armaments in various countries, the tragic scene of the partition of our country will soon be upon us. We are alarmed that a major disaster is imminent. For the medical community to actively train in battlefield rescue techniques in order to contribute, is certainly essential. However, military medical training is even more urgent. This is because the obligations of military doctors are not limited to wartime service, but also have a great responsibility for the prevention and treatment of diseases among soldiers during peacetime. In the summer of the 23rd year, Mr. Lu Zhide, the director of the military medical office, separately mobilized military doctors of all levels from various places to Nanchang for refresher training. He also adopted the method of training officers in the marching camp, giving military doctors the opportunity to supplement their knowledge and temper their physique, which was indeed a valuable and meaningful move. This not only benefits the soldiers with welfare but also cultivates the inherent demeanor of military doctors. We further hope that military doctors can continue to practice this every year without interruption, which will benefit the country's future and the future of public health.

(IX) A Glimpse of the Old Medical Field

In the 23rd year, the old medical field can be said to be filled with a smoky atmosphere: the Ephedra trend that was popular in Shanghai was even more unbearable. What caused the Ephedra trend? The newspapers were in an uproar, seeming to attribute it to the monopoly of a certain cooperative; however, according to people familiar with the inside story, the situation was extremely complex (please refer to the "Self-Destructive Ephedra Trend" in the third issue of the second volume of Social Medicine and Pharmaceuticals). We are not fond of discussing right and wrong, and the truth of this kind of fact is not something we should inquire about. From an academic standpoint, we deeply feel that the occurrence of this Ephedra trend has fully exposed the absurdity and unreliability of the old medical theories. Even taking the use of Ephedra to replace Fritillaria as an example, some say that the properties and tastes of Ephedra and Fritillaria are similar, and their effects are the same, so they can be substituted; others say that although the properties and tastes of Ephedra and Fritillaria are the same, their effects are completely different, and they cannot be substituted. Each holds to their own opinion, and speaks with conviction. Alas, this is enough to prove that all the theories of old medicine are mostly without absolute truth! With such theories, how can we compete with modern scientific medicine without being swept away by the tide of the times?

As for the medical disputes of old doctors, they have also been endless, which is due to the deteriorating social atmosphere, what more can be said! We also deeply hope that the old medical community will urgently seek to protect their practice.

The old medical publishing industry is lifeless, the same as it was in the past! Among them, there are those who are committed to improving old medicine, but they all lack the mind to distinguish right from wrong, lack the basis and knowledge of empirical experience, and lack a good foundation in natural sciences. They only plagiarize new knowledge, connect it to old theories, and blindly lead, having already entered a wrong path, and are not enough to speak of promoting old medical theories.

In recent years, medical experts at home and abroad have been devoting themselves to the study of Chinese medicine, which is very strong! Dr. Zeng Guangfang is the most diligent researcher of Chinese medicine. Dr. Zeng is currently working at the Shanghai Natural Science Institute. According to him, "In recent years, people have known that Chinese medicine has great effects, especially ginseng, which is considered to have a cardiotonic effect, but what are the ingredients of ginseng? What is its pharmacology? We do not know. This is not something that cannot be known; because to study a drug, a few or a few dozen grams are not enough as research material, one must use dozens or hundreds of kilograms. Just imagine using a hundred kilograms of ginseng, the value has reached millions. Looking around, the domestic medical and pharmaceutical field is desolate, so how can we talk about studying ginseng?" Dr. Zeng spoke with sincerity and earnestness, and we should know what to realize. Over the past year, those in the old medical field who talked about studying Chinese medicine, claiming that a certain drug has been extracted and a certain drug has clear ingredients, are simply daydreaming and cannot be relied upon.

There is one more thing that deserves our attention, that is, the deformed development of old medical education is still developing. In this transitional period, we dare not say that old medical schools cannot be established, nor dare we say that old medical practitioners cannot participate in social activities, as this is the right of citizens, and no one dares to剥削 it; however, in terms of the education system, old medical schools should not be included in the ranks of universities. In the winter of the 23rd year, at the independent college games held in Shanghai, a certain old medical school also participated openly due to its school qualifications. Implicitly, it has already been recognized that the old medical school is one of the modern Chinese universities. The educational authorities cannot but pay attention to this chaos in China's educational system.

Etiological Treatment and Prevention of Periodontitis

— Lin Jianxian

Periodontitis (Pyorrhea Alveolaris) is one of the common diseases of the oral cavity. There are many sufferers, and the harm is severe. The pus that flows out, swallowed into the gastrointestinal tract, can cause diseases in all parts of the body, such as arthritis, gastric ulcer, intestinal ulcer, pneumonia, tonsillitis, purulent pharyngitis, jaundice, gallstones, enteritis and various stomatitis. At the same time, the gums are inflamed and swollen, the teeth are loose, pus often flows, and the oral cavity is very smelly, which is disgusting. If the disease is prolonged and not treated, it will inevitably affect health, cause mental fatigue, make the face sallow and the body thin. As the disease progresses, the teeth fall out and chewing becomes difficult. According to a certain American doctor, more teeth are lost due to this disease than due to cavities. Therefore, this disease is the most worthy of attention among dental diseases. After diagnosis, I have written this article based on what I have seen and heard, and with reference to the most effective treatments that have been scattered in various books and magazines in recent years, to contribute to those who care about their health.

Etiology

There are many sources of periodontitis, which can be divided into six categories:

(1) The teeth are unevenly arranged, the bite is incorrect, or the bridges and dentures are not properly fitted. Therefore, chewing is inconvenient, and the teeth are gradually injured due to excessive and uneven pressure, resulting in this disease.

(2) Due to the lime content contained in saliva and residual food, it adheres to the gingival area, or the waste matter excreted in the blood surrounds the tooth cells (Calculus), thus irritating the gums and causing inflammation. The gums separate from the teeth to form a pocket, and the tooth line and dirt accumulate more and more. At the same time, the periodontal membrane and alveolar bone are also injured and destroyed.

(3) After the gums are inflamed and separated, pus bacteria and parasites take the opportunity to invade and wreak havoc.

(4) Drug poisoning, such as oral medications containing mercury and uric acid.

(5) Poor oral hygiene, lack of brushing, and love of eating hard objects.

(6) Systemic diseases such as venereal disease, lung disease, diabetes, etc.

Periodontitis can be divided into three types: A, B, and C.

Type A periodontitis This type of disease is less severe. The symptoms are redness, swelling, and inflammation of the gums around the neck of the tooth. This is because many excretions from saliva or blood form hard black tartar, which adheres to the tooth area and between the alveolar spaces, forming a ring. This irritates the gums, resulting in redness and swelling. However, the gums do not form pockets, or if they do, they are very shallow. Pus may or may not be present. In most cases, it is absent. The inner surface of the mandibular incisors and the outer surface of the maxillary molars are most prone to tartar. The patient's oral condition shows neglect of cleanliness and hygiene.

Type B periodontitis This is true periodontitis. The symptoms of gingivitis are not very obvious. The gums are not only not congested, but appear anemic. The gums separate from the teeth and recede. The periodontal membrane is destroyed very quickly. At the same time, the alveolar bone is damaged and shortened. The pockets are deeper. It is often found between the incisors or molar alveolar spaces. Pus flows out constantly. The oral cavity is very smelly. Hard tartar may or may not be present. The teeth are loose and eventually fall out.

Type C periodontitis This disease is mostly caused by systemic diseases, such as venereal disease, lung disease, actinomycosis, osteomyelitis, diabetes, drooling, phosphorus poisoning, malnutrition, and metabolic diseases. The symptoms also vary depending on the cause. For example, if it is caused by venereal disease, tuberculosis, and osteomyelitis, the alveolar bone is severely destroyed and progresses very quickly. Therefore, the teeth are loose. Hard tartar is often found around the teeth. Pus is constantly flowing. It takes a long time to treat before it can gradually recover. If it is caused by diabetes, the gums are swollen and painful, the periodontal membrane is inflamed, and sensitivity is excessive. Tartar formed by blood is found around the teeth. Pus may or may not be present. If it is caused by metabolic diseases, the symptoms are erratic.

Treatment Methods

(1) General Discussion

The treatment methods for periodontitis are quite complicated and require a long period of time and careful attention to be effective. The following points must be understood and noted by both the patient and the doctor to avoid failure.

(1) The patient must cooperate closely with the doctor, absolutely obey the doctor's instructions, and pay attention to everything in order to obtain permanent results.

(2) If pus is swallowed into the stomach and absorbed into the blood, it is easy to cause systemic diseases or even blood poisoning, which has a very significant impact on health. However, patients often pay little attention to pus and are only worried about the loosening and falling out of their teeth. The doctor should pay attention to this kind of psychology.

(3) If the root tip has not changed, proper treatment can stop the pus and restore the health of the teeth. However, the effectiveness of the teeth will be inferior to that before the disease.

(4) If there are severe symptoms that cannot be cured in fact, it is best to extract the teeth as a last resort. There is no need to go through a long period of treatment, which is futile and disappointing for the patient.

(5) Regarding daily diet and hygiene, patients should drink more water. Slightly alkaline beverages such as soda, fruit seeds, and salt are also beneficial if consumed occasionally. In addition, the bowels should not be constipated. Eat more fruits, vegetables, and brown rice to stimulate the stomach and intestines. Eat less sugar cakes and refined pastries. Rinse your mouth immediately after eating.

(6) The treatment methods for periodontitis can be divided into three types, namely surgical operation, drug treatment, and instrument installation.

Common Sense of Hygiene for the Ear, Nose, Throat, and Eyes

— Tang Renjin

(31) Scarlet Fever

Naming - Scarlet fever is called Scharlach by Germans and Scarlet Fever by the British. In the past, China had never heard of anything called scarlet fever. There is no record of this disease in ancient medical books. It is not even known that it is an infectious disease. The general public thought that the rashes of this disease were quite similar to measles, so they were often confused and called measles (or red measles). From the perspective of Chinese medicine, because this disease mostly combines with throat symptoms, the different names of throat measles, measles throat, rotten throat measles, and rotten throat 疔 measles are generally used. In fact, what he is discussing are all referring to scarlet fever. (To be continued)

A Simple Explanation of Pulmonary Tuberculosis (37)

— Hu Jiayan

The detailed circumstances of the five types of tuberculin tests have been described above. As for their true diagnostic value, as estimated by theory, a brief account may be given here. Firstly, we must understand that their diagnostic assistance in determining whether or not the patient has this disease is, of course, undeniable. As for the current condition, such as whether it is still progressing or has reached a state of arrest, the extent of the disease, and the size of the affected area, these are far less accurate and reliable than physical examination and X-ray fluoroscopy! Secondly, considering only whether or not it is this disease, the value of a negative reaction is greater than that of a positive reaction. Regarding positive reactions, their application to children is greater than to adults. We must understand that almost no one can escape the transmission of tuberculosis. Even those who are disease-free throughout their lives were certainly infected in their infancy, which can be proven by autopsy. Therefore, even if a positive reaction is found, it is possible in everyone who has been infected, and its diagnostic value for the current disease is understandably reduced! According to this theory, a negative reaction can put an end to the suspicion of the disease being present. As for the comparison between children and adults, this can also be inferred from this!

Finally, in recent times, some people have also been engaged in autogenous urine reaction tests. The test procedure involves injecting several drops of the patient's own urine intradermally to observe the local reaction. In addition, there are similar tests for autogenous serum and autogenous sweat. However, their diagnostic value has not yet been determined, so it is better to omit them here to avoid being verbose!

Free Talk

Mark Twain, the Scourge of American Citizens

— Li Bo

From a barefoot, wild boy working in Hannibal, to liberation from colonial status, a Mississippi boatman, a wanderer for many years who reached the highest position in American literature, Mark Twain, it is exactly one hundred years since his birth.

Before Mark Twain, we could say that America had no literature of its own. It is true that we know America had Hawthorne, Irving, and Poe, but these people were merely imitators of British literature, inheritors of the British tradition. The literature they created was not truly American, but merely a tributary of British literature. They sought to cater not to domestic readers, but to London critics. They depicted not the rough and bold pioneers of the wilderness, but the delicate and restrained gentlemen of the salons.

However, the citizens who had only recently been liberated were ultimately unable to be satisfied with this. Moreover, nature was so generous to them: they had a mild climate, vast prairies, mysterious virgin forests, the magnificent Mississippi, the bountiful Californian gold mines, cheap slave labor, and the promising prospects for industrial and commercial development. Their world was one of gold and joy. They needed the adventurous spirit of the pioneers, and they also needed laughter, even if it was shallow laughter, as long as it was fresh and lively, which was exactly what they demanded.

They also demanded to search the world with the keen eyes of a newly released hunting dog, and to criticize everything with light satire.

The first to satisfy these demands, no, the first to reflect this new consciousness, was Mark Twain. His early masterpieces, filled with light-hearted jokes, "The Celebrated Jumping Frog," and his travelogue with its novel perspective, "Innocents Abroad," were able to quickly seize a wide readership in farmhouses and taverns, achieving sales like the Bible, which was by no means accidental.

Mark Twain himself was a fresh and vigorous figure. His personality and his style were symbols of America at that time. On May 10, 1870, precisely when his "Innocents Abroad" achieved its widest sales, and three months after his marriage to Miss Olivia Langdon, he wrote in a letter to Nevada that he had "a lovely wife; a lovely house, the house with charming decorations; a lovely carriage; and a coachman with a demeanor of awe-inspiring charm—nothing is lacking, and I earn more money than I really need." This was the prosperity of a Nevada miner in debt, wasn't it the free America that had been liberated from colonial status, passed through the Civil War, and obtained a free labor market?

He stepped into literature with the vigorous force of the frontier and the harmony of humor, expressing the adventurous spirit of the early settlers entirely in his own rough, often misspelled words, according to his own keen eyes. He also gave new evaluations to everything in Europe. He broke away from tradition, abandoned authority, and no dogma could bind his restless passion and light satire in the slightest.

"What does he satirize, this literary darling of the newly rising citizen nation?" Perhaps there is such an inquiry.

Although it was a newly rising citizen nation, it had old dregs and new developing problems. Therefore, there were truly many targets for the satire of our philosopher of laughter. He had literary prisoners such as Addison, Lamb, Milton, and Carlyle, and even more, he had the superintendent of the village Sunday school, children who had learned hundreds of Bible lessons, Christian scientists who praised Mrs. Eddy, stubborn Shakespeare experts, relic seekers, connoisseurs who guessed that they would be appreciated according to general principles, people who arrogantly quoted famous people's "last words," Americans who flattered the rich, tens of thousands of humble people who only had words and no actions, shameless journalists who raped people's homes with their newspapers, theologians who were certain, stubborn "scientific" boasters, sentimentalists who held grand celebrations during mourning, anarchists of behavior, professors who always quoted the words of other professors, people who got rich quickly, people who got smart quickly, and religious reformers.

Among all the social phenomena he mocked, he showed the greatest disrespect to religion. He said that Christian civilization was a civilization of killing, that the invention of the sharpest weapons was Christianity's most worthy victory, and he said, "In the second or third century, we will certainly see that all qualified murderers are Christians." In his "The $30,000 Bequest," there is an interesting description: "These are three cold days when she loads the goods of the gospel onto the ship, which is to persuade the shallow Chinese to exchange twenty-four pure gold Confucian doctrines for counterfeit Christianity.

Just as he opposed all biased social phenomena, Mark Twain's anti-religion was somewhat rough and shallow. He did not know that Christian civilization could no longer exist in the "second or third century." However, there is no doubt that his spirit grasped the progressive consciousness of the early citizen society.

Smile (4)

— Written by Lamernce of England, translated by Tang Xiru

They had no children, and he was often sadly in need of children, which made him feel very sad.

Now she would never return to him, this was the thirteenth time, she was gone forever.

But was this her? As he thought this, he felt her lightly touching somewhere on his ribs, making him smile. He frowned, and a look of anger appeared on his face. He stopped smiling! As he looked down at this infinitely infuriating dead woman, he clenched his square, exposed gums, revealing his large teeth. "It's like this again!"—he really wanted to say to her like a character in a Dickens novel.

He himself had never learned well, and he was prepared to let his many shortcomings remain.

He suddenly turned back to the three women, who had retreated into the shadows beyond the candlelight, and were now hovering between him and something, wearing their white headscarves. His eyes shone, and he bared his teeth.

"The sin is mine! The sin is mine!" he suddenly shouted loudly.

"Macche!" the frightened abbess cried out, quickly extending her hands, and then tucking them back into her sleeves, like a pair of small birds roosting together in a nest.

Matthew nodded his head, staring blankly around, ready to run out. The abbess was chanting a hymn softly behind him, her rosary swinging. The pale young nun retreated further back, but the robust, black, thoughtful nun, like a perpetually humorous star, stared at him from above, and he felt the smile tickling him in his ribs again.

"Listen!" he advised the women, "I am being strangely abnormal now, I think I'd better leave."

Distinguishing Characters and Distinguishing Words (3)

— Cao Juren

Host—Good, let's start with Su Xun and Su Zhe's Six States essays. The Selections of Ancient Prose includes Su Xun's "On Power" (Six States), with three circles added under the title (circles were added under the title of the Selections of Ancient Prose to distinguish between good and bad). Liu Haifeng commented, "The force of the brush is simple and old." Su Zhe's "On Six States" has two circles added under the title. A comment on the eyebrow of the Xu family edition from Xiao County says, "Familiar with the situation at the time." It can be seen that these two "On Six States" essays were originally most praised by the predecessors of the Tongcheng School. The historical facts of the Six States are there. We will discuss history based on history. Which of Su Xun and Su Zhe's arguments is nonsense that we can agree with? Why did the Six States decline? Why was Qin able to unify? From a national perspective, this was an inevitable trend after a mixture matured. From the early Zhou Dynasty to the Spring and Autumn Period, from the Spring and Autumn Period to the Warring States Period, the big fish ate the small fish, and the big bugs ate the small bugs. The ebb and flow, rise and fall of various tribes and feudal lords never stopped for a single day. The decline of the Six States was no different from the process of decline of the eight hundred feudal lords. Qin's strength and unification were no different from the strength and partial unification of the seven heroes of the Warring States Period. From an economic perspective, the development of the agricultural economy determined the national fortune of a country. Since Shang Yang took power in Qin, he implemented private land ownership and rewarded large-scale production. Qin invaded the Six States, where agricultural production was backward (the nobility occupied the land, and the production methods were backward), with the wealthy Guanzhong region. The outcome of the battle was obvious. In terms of political thought and organization, Confucianism, Mohism, and Legalism all tended toward a political view of centralized power, sufficient food, and strong soldiers. The Six States' power was held by the nobility, and nothing could be reformed in a planned way. The Legalists were in power in Qin, reducing the power of the wealthy and concentrating power in the central government, implementing a plan for sufficient food and strong soldiers, naturally invincible and conquering all. Did Su Xun and Su Zhe's "On Six States" even scratch the itch at all? They said: "The destruction of the Six States was not because their weapons were not sharp or their battles were not well fought, but because of bribery to Qin. Bribery to Qin depleted their strength, and this was the path to destruction!" (Su Xun, "On Six States") And: "What Qin was competing with the feudal lords for the world was not in Qi, Chu, Yan, and Zhao, but on the outskirts of Han and Wei; what the feudal lords were competing with Qin for the world was not in Qi, Chu, Yan, and Zhao, but in the wilderness of Han and Wei... Han and Wei were a barrier for the feudal lords, but they allowed the Qin people to enter and exit between them. How could they know the situation of the world?" (Su Zhe, "On Six States") Isn't this as childish as an elementary school student's desk history essay? Would modern young people who have read a little cultural history and social history make such ridiculous arguments? It is no wonder that in the Jiawu year (1894), a censor with a Hanlin background wanted to memorialize the throne, saying, "To the north of Japan, there are two great powers, Siam and Burma, which are wealthy and have strong soldiers. I ask that the Emperor send envoys to establish good relations and attack Japan from the north and south to seal its fate." If you are willing to compare the essays of modern young people carefully with the essays of the Eight Great Masters of the Tang and Song Dynasties, you will feel that in all aspects, whether philosophy, society, or nature, they are much more advanced, at least more accurate.

Guest—In that case, please compare them from the aspect of organization:

Host—Ancient Chinese literati only had literary collections. Literary collections are like existing magazines, talking about everything under the sky and above the earth, contradicting themselves before and after, with very little organization. The pre-Qin philosophers were relatively more organized. Only Zhuangzi, Xunzi, and Han Fei can be said to have clear and coherent systems. After the Qin and Han Dynasties, only Wang Chong's "Lunheng," Liu Xie's "Wen Xin Diao Long," Liu Zhiji's "Shi Tong," and Zhang Xuecheng's "Wen Shi Tong Yi" were relatively more organized. Even a great writer like Wang Zhong's "Shuxue" was just a mixed platter and could not be said to be organized. For example, Han Yu's "Yuandao" is precisely "Confucian words are not enough, so he resorts to arrogant pretense, wandering wildly, trampling on crops and vegetables, and ultimately making mistakes in several articles." (Zhang Taiyan's words) Han Yu fundamentally did not understand the claims of Taoism, nor did he understand the claims of Buddhism, and even less did he understand the similarities and differences between Taoism and Buddhism. In short, he was not even very clear about the claims of Confucianism; therefore, he could not organize a complete theory, and he could not write a complete article. Even a famous article like "Yuandao" is so incoherent, not to mention those mediocre ancient prose. No matter how undesirable modern young people are, at least they have received a little logical training and read some European and American papers, and they will never contradict themselves like Han Yu. There is no need to say anything else. If you just look at those writers of the Tongcheng School, can any writer be as meticulous as Yan Fu or as vivid as Lin Shu? Moreover, does Lin Shu himself have any works that are as good as his own translations? Furthermore, when Zhang Shizhao lectures on literary editing, his articles have vitality; once he delves into the horns of a dilemma and tries to restore the past, nine out of ten of his articles are incomprehensible. Adding another "moreover," all those who have been baptized by Western literature show their characteristics. (Zhang Taiyan's essays are deeply influenced by Buddhism and did not come from ancient prose of the Tang and Song Dynasties.) Therefore, in terms of organization, modern young people are also much more advanced than others, at least more meticulous than the ancient prose masters of the Tang and Song Dynasties.

Guest—Your high regard for the present and your suppression of the past are certainly justifiable and reasonable; but I am still not very clear as to why reading the articles of the ancients always feels much better than the articles of the present people.

Host—This is your traditional thinking at work! Mr. Tang Bohuang said it well: "The ancient is elegant, and the present is vulgar, which is human nature. The more ancient something is, the more elegant it seems. Writing cannot escape this example. The reasons for this are complex: one is due to the rarity of ancient objects: things that are rare are treasured, and things that are treasured are elegant. Ritual vessels are like this, and so is writing. The second is due to the fact that later generations often idealize the past; we do not see the ancients, and we often imagine their lives to be ideal; therefore, the golden age must be in ancient times. The third is due to the fact that the language of modern people, because it is commonly used in daily life, often makes us associate with concrete situations in the present world—many unsatisfactory and impure things. The writing of the ancients, because it is different from the current language, does not produce such associations, so we feel that it is relatively less vulgar. This psychological effect of 'the ancient is elegant and the present is vulgar' often makes you feel that reading the articles of the ancients is much better than the articles of the present people. Excuse me for telling a joke, when you feel that the articles of the ancients are particularly good, you really haven't understood the articles of the ancients yet! The predecessors did not understand the "Book of Documents" and regarded "Pan Geng" as a treasured article; modern people do not understand the eight-legged essay, and some people also regard that kind of stinking and mediocre tune as a good article; once they understand it, they will not love that damn thing! The times are always advancing. If I were an ancient person, I would certainly hope that the articles of later generations would be more advanced than mine. Each generation should be better than the last, and this is the main road for cultural progress. If the Chinese language proficiency of modern young people is really declining day by day, each generation being worse than the last, and later generations all become fools, what glory is there for the ancients?

A Man and a Woman

— Xu Ying

Early morning.

Before I even reached the bridgehead, I saw the riverbank crowded with a dark mass of people. When I reached the bridgehead, I couldn't help but stop and, amid the noisy, laughing voices of the people, cast my gaze at the same focal point as they did.

This river is a tributary of the Daqing River, commonly called the Xiaoqing River. The water is extremely clean, clear, and bright, with lines of ripples chasing each other, flowing slowly in the deep brown, not very wide riverbed, always so leisurely. The morning sun reflected the centipede boats moored near the bridgehead, leaving extremely soft, snake-like shadows in the heart of the water. In the distance, a very large corpse floated up and down, like a skinned cow.

A variety of voices arose from the crowd:

"Could it be that the upstream has flooded again—the river water is not muddy...?"

"How could that be a person, a person is not that big...?"

"How could there be someone so silly, livestock that fall into the river are not fed to people...?"

More and more people gathered at the bridgehead and along the bank. From the east of the river and the west of the river, this was an important transportation route. Those carrying poles and those carrying baskets, one by one with their yellow mud legs and wearing pale, shimmering cloth shirts, crowded to make way. Those behind asked those in front: "What's going on? Did someone jump into the river!" The people in front did not answer, but squeezed even harder.

In the middle of the river, the corpse followed the current, breaking the ripples and rising and falling. Closer, it was clear. At this time, the faces of the young lads turned red, and they smiled, unexpectedly exclaiming:

"Hey—a man and a woman!"

The faces of the women standing on the bow of the centipede boat watching the excitement also turned red, and they spat out a mouthful of saliva, but they still looked back greedily for another hard look, and then successively turned into the cabin, shouting at their children, cat or dog, "Come in, come in, don't dirty your eyes!"

"This is really what a world," an old man sighed, "to produce such a disgrace!"

I saw the corpse gradually flowing towards the bridge. It was indeed so, a man and a woman were tightly tied together, facing each other. The corpses had been in the water for quite some time, and the river water had permeated into every cell of their bodies. The people were swollen like cows. As a rule, floating corpses flow on their backs, but now, because the balance of the two people was inconsistent, slightly agitated on the water's surface, they would turn over.

"Heh-heh-heh." Every young person was happy. "They're still moving!"

The corpses slowly passed through the heart of the river among the centipede boats. People were noisily discussing the reasons for the crime of these two young people. People were all standing with their hands in their sleeves, and no one proposed to rescue or bury them. I knew that this kind of thing was close to "bad luck". Boatmen were sometimes afraid of breaking their good fortune. If it were a single person, there would certainly have been philanthropists already.

The corpse reached the side of the bridge. The man's face was facing upwards. Seeing that face, a familiar shock in my memory, yes, I recognized this face, although it was now swollen and pale. When I saw the scar on his forehead, I knew it was him, although for a moment, I could not call out his name.

So I hurriedly squeezed down from the bridgehead to find You Er, You Er, this old boatman, had already died without an heir. I thought that he probably wouldn't mind this kind of thing. Finding him in the crowd, I said:

"You should accumulate some virtue, Lao Er, pull them out and find someone to bury them. Get the money from me!"

You Er put his dry tobacco pouch in his waist and agreed.

"It's the school teacher who is doing good deeds after all," some passersby praised me, "It's really not right to show these indecent things to men and women under the sun!"

The sun was high, and when I came back from the elementary school, I saw that the people were already in the coffin. You Lao Er said, "Just let them lie in one coffin." At this time, I saw the woman's face clearly again. I understood in my heart that I not only recognized the man, but I also recognized this woman. They were my first students when I was running a community school upstream of the Daqing River, and they were also my helpers.

Supplement to the Shen Bao Local Edition

Talks

China is China of the World

— Tie Di

According to a Reuters dispatch, Professor Boschmann of Germany is coming to China to study ancient Chinese architecture. Professor Boschmann is a scholar specializing in architectural studies. He came to China before 1909, and then came to China again in 1933 to begin his research on China. On January 8th, he returned to his country on the "Saarbrücken," having spent fifteen months visiting thirteen provinces. Half of his research was on ancient Chinese architecture, especially religious architecture, particularly temples and pagodas, and half was on the innovation and transformation of Chinese architecture in a changing era. He also studied Chinese farmers and their residences, observing new and old art, especially urban architecture.

From the above news, it seems that it is something to rejoice about. Why is that? Some people think that our country's architecture is indeed progressing. For example, Professor Boschmann's coming to China can be taken as a good example. In fact, it is not so.

Is our country's architecture really progressing? No. On the surface, although Western-style buildings of more than ten or twenty stories have appeared, in fact, these achievements do not completely belong to us. The representatives of imperialist countries are still in the position of guidance. In other words, all the rights are being manipulated in their hands.

Then, since we understand these meanings, what is Professor Boschmann here for? In short, he is also a representative of the imperialists. His purpose in studying Chinese architecture is not to provide him with research materials, but to imitate all the phenomena of our country's architecture, in order to plan everything, in other words, to plan for future monopoly!

In this changing era, imperialism feels that it is about to be shaken, so they are mutually exclusive, pushing and snatching from each other. As a result, they cannot achieve victory in this environment, and thus they develop madly towards colonies or semi-colonies, hoping to find something ideal for them in this arena.

What is Professor Boschmann's mission in coming to China? Of course, he cannot escape the atmosphere of imperialism. Therefore, it can be seen that his mission in coming to China has great significance. From this, everyone also feels that China is China of the world!

Winter

— Dai Ni

The winter evening is lonely.

Returning from the field, dusk crawls into every corner of the small room. I'm too lazy to flip the light switch – in fact, turning on the sixteen-candlepower electric light would only accentuate the dimness of dusk, making one feel a low, oppressive atmosphere. I take off my winter coat and throw my tired body onto the sofa, stretching out my legs like a traveler arriving at a small inn, needing only rest.

No thoughts, eyes vaguely closed, isolating all sounds from my hearing, but not quite asleep. If someone were to burst in as if I were expecting them, I would be able to jump up the moment their foot stepped inside.

But I dare not hope, for the winter evening is lonely; there is no fireplace with roaring flames here, no rich coffee, and certainly no charming woman, like the life in high-rise buildings, passing the winter evening in an atmosphere full of springtime.

Though I say there are no thoughts, my mind, like an annoying creditor, barges in mercilessly: I remember when we had a brazier.

It was midnight, with heavy snow falling, when I eloped with my lover, fleeing the feudal forces that permeated our hometown like poisonous flames. We ran without stopping all night, and at daybreak, we arrived at a friend's house – three thatched huts in a small village.

Brushing off the thick layer of snow that weighed us down, we collapsed into bamboo chairs beside the brazier. Our bodies were so tired they could no longer support us, but our spirits were excited. We toasted bread to stave off hunger, and our faces, illuminated by the firelight, smiled at each other; I remember being startled out of the silence only when the flames burned our feet.

In this way, we spent every winter evening beside the brazier. But this enjoyment, like winter, was driven away by the god of spring when the swallows returned.

Since then, I have had no home. With wounded feet, I have traveled all over the country, spending countless lonely winter evenings.

This unforgettable image immediately reappears before my eyes as I rest, so I open my eyes to find darkness. Only the rhythmic sound of a wandering monk's wooden fish drum approaches from afar. Wanderer, what do you seek?

I rise from the darkness, groping for the light switch on the wall. The light from the sixteen candles casts my elongated shadow outside the door, like a hibernating snake.

Looking into the dark corridor, I desperately hope for an uninvited guest to share my pointless worries. Even if it were truly a creditor, I would treat them as an honored guest, but this hope, like the sound of the wooden fish drum, tells me – this world is empty.

From one corner to the other, I pace back and forth, the lonely shadow flickering wildly on the four walls, as if discovering the answer to a difficult question, entrusting the lost balance of my thoughts to its movements, forgetting the faintly aching wounds on the soles of my feet.

Finally, a cold air rises from my heels to my body, and the first crowing of the rooster and the rhythmic sound of the wooden fish drum sound at the same time. I raise my distracted eyes and look out the window, a sheet of white reflected light. The roofs across the street are covered with cotton-like thick snow, and it seems as if my mind has also been swept clean. I open the window and take a deep breath of cold air.

"Another lonely winter night has passed!" I mutter to myself.

"But what about this evening's dusk?" I ask myself.

"If winter comes, can spring be far behind?" a voice answers me.

But spring, ah, is the season when the swallows return!

Heavenly Kingdom on the South Sea

— San Lang

"Doumen is a heavenly kingdom facing the South Sea!"

The name Doumen is so enchanting. It is a small island in the South Sea, a ten-hour boat trip from Macau. Last year, I wandered there.

Doumen is indeed as miraculous as I imagined! High, overlapping mountain peaks winding along. Seen from the sea, it is a beautiful painting, with enchanting scenery, semi-tropical forests, lush and thriving, containing a gentle and lovely atmosphere, permeating the heart of a traveler with a sad melody.

Although Doumen does not have the grand buildings of a metropolis, nor the dark scenes of prostitutes, it everywhere reveals the wounds of being ravaged by soldiers! It deeply stirred my thoughts! Look, this small island

Page 20

The people inside have not lost their freedom, nor their desire to live. It was just after a drought, and everything planted had withered. The harvest was small. But the soldiers still increased the river protection tax by six cents per mu. Heavens! Their lives are screaming in the hands of the executioners of tyranny. In Doumen, I heard an old man tell the story of Doumen:

"More than ten years ago, this place was still a kingdom of pirates. The soldiers had no way to deal with them, because the pirates were mostly locals, brave and fierce, willing to do anything, even risk their lives, for food. The war lasted for several years, with both sides having warships. It was really exciting. However, it eventually calmed down, and a new batch of soldiers came, making the lives of the common people even more miserable. All kinds of levies and taxes! After the harvest, a large portion of the grain had to be taken away. Such a life is not as good as it was more than ten years ago."

The people of Doumen are all sighing. The hurried tone, the painful roar, gave me an indelible and profound impression:

"Doumen on the South Sea is no longer a heavenly kingdom!"

The countryside of Doumen is so beautiful, with few modern buildings. The people's way of life still retains the old ways. However, this small island has already opened up several long roads, connecting the east, west, north, and south of the island. There are also many old-fashioned cars roaring and running. However, the people in the countryside no longer feel any surprise. They have been influenced by the big cities. They have tasted many different flavors. They have long been whipped by the exploiters from the cities. They have found courage in a painful life. What they demand is life. In the past few years, Doumen has seen many instances of hand-to-hand combat between the common people and the soldiers. When I traveled there, it was just after a fierce bloody fight. The deep wounds were still so clearly before my eyes.

Although Doumen is a small island filled with enchanting atmosphere, with beautiful scenery and lovely, spirited people, I ultimately left with a disappointed tone.

"Doumen is no longer a heavenly kingdom on the South Sea. Everywhere reveals the wounds of having been ravaged."

On the Great River

— Liang Qijun

A large flock of ducks drifts downstream along the riverbank; Old Fan, who herds the ducks, sits in a large wooden tub, following behind, commanding them. These drifting people of the rivers and lakes drift along with the ducks!

It is already dusk.

The vast mountain range, pressed down by the dim sky, stands in the increasingly thick twilight, hanging its head. A not-so-dense swarm of black dots spreads across the mountain range; it is a flock of crows returning to their nests, their loud, abrupt cries left in the sky, echoing and lingering. Ah, the cries of the returning birds are so melancholic, so mournful in the ears of this wanderer!

Because in this lonely space, this lonely space filled with twilight, besides the returning birds, the mountain range, the ducks, and a lone duck herder; there is only the river singing a flowing melody, accompanied by the slightly chilly evening wind of late autumn. Therefore, this occasional cry, to him—this drifter of the rivers and lakes—at least, will feel a little comfort, a little warmth.

The mountain range drifted past.

Next, a stretch of withered yellow grassland unfolds ahead. In the distant border, the dim sky and the monotonous withered yellow are separated only by a not-so-obvious, blurry black line.

On the shore over there, farther away, there is still an unbroken mountain range; however, the darkness of dusk has begun to swallow them.

Therefore, the heart of this drifting Old Fan is filled with melancholy, sorrow, and an inexplicable emptiness. Just like the twilight that permeates the vast river surface and the vast sky.

One or two ducks strayed from the flock, and he busily used a bamboo pole to drive them back. This flock of ignorant ducks quietly and docilely listens to the "march" of the river.

In the distant harbor, a few masts stand in the blur. In the haze, a few faint lights tremble. Seeing that the place of return is about to be reached, this lost and lonely heart then rises with eager hope.

Suddenly, I feel excited.

That bright place of return!

The rest that the drifter has tired of all day has appeared like dawn.

Making a Home

— Fang

Mentioning the words "making a home" now seems rather corrupt and ridiculous. The meaning of the words "making a home" is to be thrifty and economical. Speaking of making a home, I think of such a thing.

In *The Scholars*, Yan Jiansheng earned more than a hundred thousand in family wealth. When he was dying, phlegm went in and out of his throat. One sound after another, he could not take his last breath. He took his hand out of the blanket, stretched out two fingers, and no one around him could guess his meaning. Only his concubine, Zhao, knew what was on his mind. She picked off one of the two lamp wicks burning in the lamp. Only then did Yan Jiansheng feel relieved, nodded, let his hand fall, and immediately lost his breath.

There is an old lady in my hometown who is almost eighty or ninety years old this year. In her early years, she lacked food and clothing and was extremely poor. Now she has actually taught her children to become famous and has also accumulated hundreds of thousands in family wealth. She has two maxims for managing a home: "What teaches what is embarrassing, what teaches what doesn't care about this." These two sentences seem extremely ordinary at first glance, but when you savor them carefully, they contain great truth. What is called "what teaches what is embarrassing" refers to all expenses. Expenses should naturally be saved if they can be saved. If they cannot be saved, they may still be saved. Even if they must be spent, only a very small number or very small things should be given to people. People around you will definitely say that they are embarrassed, but she strongly opposes it, saying, "What teaches what is embarrassing." What is called "what teaches what doesn't care about this" refers to all income. No matter how small, she is unwilling to give it up easily. People around you will definitely say that they don't care about this, but she will never agree, saying, "What teaches what doesn't care about this."

These two methods of making a home are indeed too mean and too ridiculous, but in the past, many families did start like this, because people in the past were very frugal with themselves and did not desire extravagance. Therefore, the ancients had a saying, "If you earn a thousand coins and spend more than a thousand coins, you are poor even if you are rich. If you earn one coin and spend less than one coin, you are rich even if you are poor." Now is the world of social interaction and material civilization. Luxury is the prevailing custom. If you still do this, it is like "walking with a saw, cutting off a step with every step." You absolutely cannot do it.

Modern thoughts and environment are absolutely different from the past. Material desires are very high, and life seeks comfort, so in general, the mind only thinks of ease, leisure, beauty, fashion, Western-style houses and cars, high officials and generous salaries, and beautiful wives and concubines, circling in the mind every day. These extravagant desires are naturally not easy to achieve. Therefore, those with weak ambitions become bored, depressed, depressed, trapped, passive, and suicidal. Those with strong willpower take risks and commit crimes. Nothing is impossible. Therefore, young people living in the present era are really in great danger. The temptation of the environment, the greatness of hope, and the road of life are becoming narrower and narrower. Therefore, for modern young people, there is only to cut off desires and bury oneself in hard work in order to have a way out. As the saying goes, "One must suffer hardship in order to be above others," otherwise, it is a dead end.

Lost

— Ronin

A red-hot heart born from the earth, but now, it is lost on the human journey.

Carrying this active heart, along with the body given by my mother, I have walked through the world. I have endured thorns, crossed vast deserts, and climbed over high mountains. But what has humanity given me? What taste has the world brought me?

The world shows me a cruel face, and humanity shows me a cold countenance. The red-hot heart is killed by the sharp thorns of life, and the bright red blood is sucked dry by society.

What remains is loneliness and solitude – a specimen of a heart squeezed dry.

I have repeatedly tried to break the dark knots that surround me, regardless of the consequences; but the knots become tighter and tighter. I have also resisted that brutal face with all my heart and soul, but the menacing face comes closer and closer...

Every time: one disillusionment has just passed, and another setback comes. The darkness is like a bottomless abyss, and the sandbars spread out before my eyes are so vast that they have no end.

In the sorrow of failure, I lost my courage. In repeated stumbles, I became exhausted. The hot blood has gradually cooled, and the circulation of blood seems to be nearing exhaustion.

From the wounds all over my body, I勉强爬起来, look up, and see that I am still surrounded by a boundless desert, and I cannot see a trace of light in the future. The thick fog is layered around me, and the wind and hail attack me forever.

Ah, where is the light? Where is the oasis with a spring of water!

Should I bury my hot blood and red heart in this wilderness? Or should I find a way out of this maze?

But where is the road? Where is the resource that supplies the lifeblood of my heart?

Earth, please bring the red heart you gave birth to out of the maze! Earth, your son has now become a little lamb lost in the maze!

Tears of a Camel

— Luo Jia

(Dragging its heavy steps, in the vast desert, the herd of camels forever advances on its long journey. Although the yellow sand shrouds it like fog, unable to see the green grass and clear water, the knife-like north wind, the Mongolian's strong whip, and the heavy, unbearable cargo, are all endured by the sturdy camel. With a share of perseverance, and a share of the spirit of enduring hardship, patiently, step by step, it treads over the desolate desert land. Camels have no tears, because they know that endurance is an indispensable skill.)

Once living in a mountain temple in West Lake, the young man had no home. His wandering footprints had trod through the cities of the Pearl River basin, and also trod through every alley in the ancient capital. However, what did he have? He was a homeless wanderer, driven by the whip of life, just like the journey of a camel, the power to decide was in the hands of the driver.

The soft and greasy lake wind could not hold a wanderer's heart. Finally, he was taken away by a long line of Shanghai-Hangzhou trains, and abandoned in the city colored by the neon lights. His faltering steps dragged over asphalt roads, dragged over rugged narrow lanes. Fortunately, he sold his brains at the lowest price.

The circle of life tightened the wanderer's actions, so, like a camel, in the desert-like journey of life, he allowed the long, long time to dominate the joy of his youth, and crawled, dragging his heavy steps,含着人生的苦涙, step by step, onto the desolate journey of life.

Yes, he had accepted the leather whip of life with the greatest patience. However, when he looked at himself in the mirror, gazing at his thin triangular face and his unkempt beard, he could not help but sigh. He grabbed the old blue cloth coat he was wearing, and a torch of anger was ignited. However, reality was a black iron hand, it extinguished his anger, forcing him to bow to the shackles of the current system, like a tamed lamb, hanging down his tears. These tears, he had kept for a long time, after all, he shed tears.

(The camel trudging in the desert has a share of perseverance, and a share of the spirit of enduring hardship, however, the north wind blows on its brown hair, the Mongolian's leather whip whips its legs, the heavy cargo presses all over its flesh. At this time, the camel will also shed bitter tears.)

Citizens Who Can't Queue

— Gao Han

A few days ago, I went back to ×× because of something at home. I arrived at the North Station early, before ticket sales had started. I was waiting at the window. As usual, the crowd was very congested; people were pushing and shoving to be first. Later, an announcement was made that ticket sales had begun. So, like everyone else, I挤着as if my life depended on it. I managed to buy a ticket, and like everyone else, I boarded the train as if I were in a race. Just as I grabbed a window seat, sat down, and breathed a sigh of relief, I reached into my pocket and found that my pocket watch, which I had used for four years, was gone.

Therefore, I had an unpleasant trip. I was annoyed by myself, thinking about this and that in my mind, and constantly glaring angrily at the passengers in front of me who were sitting blankly, and the vendors selling various snacks. Undoubtedly, I was treating everyone in this carriage as an enemy.

Citizens who can't queue – I seemed to mutter to myself, scolding someone in the dark.

Regarding the characteristic of Chinese people not being able to queue, I'm afraid everyone deeply feels it, right? Whether at train stations, theaters, or assembly halls – in short, in all public places, Chinese people are unwilling to maintain order and enter and exit in a "single file." Perhaps some people think this habit is unimportant; however, I see a more serious meaning in it.

"Each sweeps the snow from his own doorstep, and doesn't care about the frost on other people's roofs." These two sentences are the golden rule for Chinese people in dealing with the world. But in reality, what meaning does this contain? It is to tell you to only take care of yourself and never care about what others do. Last time, when someone was shot and killed by thugs on Avenue Joffre, it was not the victim's compatriots who went to the police station to report it, but a foreigner in our country: seeing this news in the newspaper, we cannot but be filled with emotion. And the overseas Chinese who failed miserably at the hands of organized foreign businessmen because they did not understand mutual assistance, isn't that also because of this philosophy of dealing with the world?

Some foreigners know this "problem" of the Chinese very well: so they are used to using the two methods of inciting internal strife and defeating them individually to deal with the Chinese. Please study the history of modern China's decline carefully!

But the Chinese are never willing to give up their ideas of thinking they are smart and thinking it is beneficial to themselves. If one day China were to perish, it would undoubtedly perish because of this "problem"!

And not being willing to queue, if you think about it carefully, isn't it the most obvious manifestation of this "problem"?
